<skill_content name="openspec-explore">
# Skill: openspec-explore

Enter explore mode. Think deeply. Visualize freely. Follow the conversation wherever it goes.

**IMPORTANT: Explore mode is for thinking, not implementing.** You may read files, search code, and investigate the codebase, but you must NEVER write code or implement features. If the user asks you to implement something, remind them to exit explore mode first (e.g., start a change with `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`). You MAY create OpenSpec artifacts (proposals, designs, specs) if the user asks—that's capturing thinking, not implementing.

**This is a stance, not a workflow.** There are no fixed steps, no required sequence, no mandatory outputs. You're a thinking partner helping the user explore.

---

## The Stance

- **Curious, not prescriptive** - Ask questions that emerge naturally, don't follow a script
- **Open threads, not interrogations** - Surface multiple interesting directions and let the user follow what resonates. Don't funnel them through a single path of questions.
- **Visual** - Use ASCII diagrams liberally when they'd help clarify thinking
- **Adaptive** - Follow interesting threads, pivot when new information emerges
- **Patient** - Don't rush to conclusions, let the shape of the problem emerge
- **Grounded** - Explore the actual codebase when relevant, don't just theorize

---

## What You Might Do

Depending on what the user brings, you might:

**Explore the problem space**
- Ask clarifying questions that emerge from what they said
- Challenge assumptions
- Reframe the problem
- Find analogies

**Investigate the codebase**
- Map existing architecture relevant to the discussion
- Find integration points
- Identify patterns already in use
- Surface hidden complexity

**Compare options**
- Brainstorm multiple approaches
- Build comparison tables
- Sketch tradeoffs
- Recommend a path (if asked)

**Visualize**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│     Use ASCII diagrams liberally        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                         │
│   ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        │
│   │ State  │────────▶│ State  │        │
│   │   A    │         │   B    │        │
│   └────────┘         └────────┘        │
│                                         │
│   System diagrams, state machines,      │
│   data flows, architecture sketches,    │
│   dependency graphs, comparison tables  │
│                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Surface risks and unknowns**
- Identify what could go wrong
- Find gaps in understanding
- Suggest spikes or investigations

---

## OpenSpec Awareness

You have full context of the OpenSpec system. Use it naturally, don't force it.

### Check for context

At the start, quickly check what exists:
```bash
openspec list --json
```

This tells you:
- If there are active changes
- Their names, schemas, and status
- What the user might be working on

### When no change exists

Think freely. When insights crystallize, you might offer:

- "This feels solid enough to start a change. Want me to create one?"
  → Can transition to `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`
- Or keep exploring - no pressure to formalize

### When a change exists

If the user mentions a change or you detect one is relevant:

1. **Read existing artifacts for context**
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/proposal.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/design.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/tasks.md`
   - etc.

2. **Reference them naturally in conversation**
   - "Your design mentions using Redis, but we just realized SQLite fits better..."
   - "The proposal scopes this to premium users, but we're now thinking everyone..."

3. **Offer to capture when decisions are made**

   | Insight Type | Where to Capture |
   |--------------|------------------|
   | New requirement discovered | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Requirement changed | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Design decision made | `design.md` |
   | Scope changed | `proposal.md` |
   | New work identified | `tasks.md` |
   | Assumption invalidated | Relevant artifact |

   Example offers:
   - "That's a design decision. Capture it in design.md?"
   - "This is a new requirement. Add it to specs?"
   - "This changes scope. Update the proposal?"

4. **The user decides** - Offer and move on. Don't pressure. Don't auto-capture.

---

## What You Don't Have To Do

- Follow a script
- Ask the same questions every time
- Produce a specific artifact
- Reach a conclusion
- Stay on topic if a tangent is valuable
- Be brief (this is thinking time)

---

## Handling Different Entry Points

**User brings a vague idea:**
```
User: I'm thinking about adding real-time collaboration

You: Real-time collab is a big space. Let me think about this...

      COLLABORATION SPECTRUM
      ════════════════════════════════════════════

      Awareness          Coordination         Sync
          │                   │                 │
          ▼                   ▼                 ▼
      ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        ┌────────┐
      │Presence│         │Cursors │        │  CRDT  │
      │  "3    │         │ Multi  │        │Conflict│
      │online" │         │ select │        │  free  │
      └────────┘         └────────┘        └────────┘
          │                   │                 │
       trivial            moderate           complex

      Where's your head at?
```

**User brings a specific problem:**
```
User: The auth system is a mess

You: [reads codebase]

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │              CURRENT AUTH FLOW              │
     └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                        │
          ┌─────────────┼─────────────┐
          ▼             ▼             ▼
     ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐
     │ Google  │  │  GitHub │  │  Email  │
     │  OAuth  │  │  OAuth  │  │  Magic  │
     └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘
          │             │             │
          └─────────────┼─────────────┘
                        ▼
                  ┌───────────┐
                  │  Session  │
                  └─────┬─────┘
                        │
                        ▼
                  ┌───────────┐
                  │   Perms   │
                  └───────────┘

     I see three tangles. Which one's burning?
```

**User is stuck mid-implementation:**
```
User: /opsx:explore add-auth-system
      The OAuth integration is more complex than expected

You: [reads change artifacts]

     You're on task 4: "Implement OAuth flow"

     Let me trace what's involved...

     [draws diagram, explores options, suggests paths]

     Want to update the design to reflect this?
     Or add a spike task to investigate?
```

**User wants to compare options:**
```
User: Should we use Postgres or SQLite?

You: Generic answer is boring. What's the context?

User: A CLI tool that tracks local dev environments

You: That changes everything.

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │         CLI TOOL DATA STORAGE                  │
     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     Key constraints:
     • No daemon running
     • Must work offline
     • Single user

                  SQLite          Postgres
     Deployment   embedded ✓      needs server ✗
     Offline      yes ✓           no ✗
     Single file  yes ✓           no ✗

     SQLite. Not even close.

     Unless... is there a sync component?
```

---

## Ending Discovery

There's no required ending. Discovery might:

- **Flow into action**: "Ready to start? /opsx:new or /opsx:ff"
- **Result in artifact updates**: "Updated design.md with these decisions"
- **Just provide clarity**: User has what they need, moves on
- **Continue later**: "We can pick this up anytime"

When it feels like things are crystallizing, you might summarize:

```
## What We Figured Out

**The problem**: [crystallized understanding]

**The approach**: [if one emerged]

**Open questions**: [if any remain]

**Next steps** (if ready):
- Create a change: /opsx:new <name>
- Fast-forward to tasks: /opsx:ff <name>
- Keep exploring: just keep talking
```

But this summary is optional. Sometimes the thinking IS the value.

---

## Guardrails

- **Don't implement** - Never write code or implement features. Creating OpenSpec artifacts is fine, writing application code is not.
- **Don't fake understanding** - If something is unclear, dig deeper
- **Don't rush** - Discovery is thinking time, not task time
- **Don't force structure** - Let patterns emerge naturally
- **Don't auto-capture** - Offer to save insights, don't just do it
- **Do visualize** - A good diagram is worth many paragraphs
- **Do explore the codebase** - Ground discussions in reality
- **Do question assumptions** - Including the user's and your own

Relative paths in this skill (e.g., scripts/, reference/) are relative to this base directory.
Note: file list is sampled.

<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/vcs/index.ts</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: import { writeFileSync, chmodSync, unlinkSync } from "fs";
2: import { tmpdir } from "os";
3: import { join } from "path";
4: import type { Credential } from "../credentials/repository";
5: 
6: export interface VCSResult {
7:   success: boolean;
8:   output?: string;
9:   error?: string;
10:   port?: number;
11: }
12: 
13: export class VCS {
14:   private async execCommand(
15:     command: string[],
16:     cwd?: string,
17:     env?: Record<string, string>
18:   ): Promise<{ success: boolean; output: string; error: string }> {
19:     const proc = Bun.spawn(command, {
20:       cwd,
21:       stdout: "pipe",
22:       stderr: "pipe",
23:       env: env ? { ...process.env, ...env } : undefined,
24:     });
25: 
26:     const exitCode = await proc.exited;
27:     const stdout = await new Response(proc.stdout).text();
28:     const stderr = await new Response(proc.stderr).text();
29: 
30:     return {
31:       success: exitCode === 0,
32:       output: stdout.trim(),
33:       error: stderr.trim(),
34:     };
35:   }
36: 
37:   // Helper to inject HTTPS credentials into URL
38:   private injectHttpsCredentials(repoUrl: string, credential: Extract<Credential, { type: "https" }>): string {
39:     try {
40:       const url = new URL(repoUrl);
41:       url.username = encodeURIComponent(credential.username);
42:       url.password = encodeURIComponent(credential.password);
43:       return url.toString();
44:     } catch {
45:       // If URL parsing fails, assume it's SSH format and return as-is
46:       return repoUrl;
47:     }
48:   }
49: 
50:   // Helper to create temporary SSH key file
51:   private createTempSshKeyFile(privateKey: string): string {
52:     const tempDir = tmpdir();
53:     const keyFile = join(tempDir, `mimo-ssh-key-${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).slice(2)}`);
54:     writeFileSync(keyFile, privateKey, { mode: 0o600 });
55:     chmodSync(keyFile, 0o600);
56:     return keyFile;
57:   }
58: 
59:   // Helper to delete temporary SSH key file
60:   private deleteTempSshKeyFile(keyPath: string): void {
61:     try {
62:       unlinkSync(keyPath);
63:     } catch {
64:       // Ignore errors during cleanup
65:     }
66:   }
67: 
68:   // Helper to build SSH command for GIT_SSH_COMMAND
69:   private buildGitSshCommand(keyPath: string): string {
70:     return `ssh -i "${keyPath}" -o IdentitiesOnly=yes -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null`;
71:   }
72: 
73:   // Helper to detect if URL is SSH
74:   private isSshUrl(url: string): boolean {
75:     return url.startsWith("git@") || url.startsWith("ssh://");
76:   }
77: 
78:   // Helper to check if error is authentication-related
79:   private isAuthError(error: string, type: "https" | "ssh"): boolean {
80:     const lowerError = error.toLowerCase();
81:     
82:     // Exclude network errors first
83:     if (lowerError.includes("timeout") || 
84:         lowerError.includes("could not resolve") ||
85:         lowerError.includes("network is unreachable") ||
86:         lowerError.includes("no route to host")) {
87:       return false;
88:     }
89:     
90:     if (type === "https") {
91:       return lowerError.includes("authentication failed") ||
92:              lowerError.includes("403") ||
93:              lowerError.includes("401") ||
94:              lowerError.includes("unauthorized");
95:     } else {
96:       return lowerError.includes("permission denied") ||
97:              lowerError.includes("publickey") ||
98:              lowerError.includes("authentication") ||
99:              lowerError.includes("host key verification failed");
100:     }
101:   }
102: 
103:   // Helper to safely move files across filesystems (handles EXDEV error)
104:   // When rename fails due to cross-device link, falls back to copy+delete
105:   private async safeMove(sourcePath: string, destPath: string, isDirectory: boolean): Promise<void> {
106:     const { renameSync, cpSync, rmSync, mkdirSync, existsSync, readdirSync } = await import("fs");
107:     const { dirname, join } = await import("path");
108: 
109:     try {
110:       // Try rename first (fastest for same filesystem)
111:       renameSync(sourcePath, destPath);
112:     } catch (error: any) {
113:       // If error is cross-device link, fall back to copy+delete
114:       if (error.code === "EXDEV" || error.message?.includes("cross-device")) {
115:         // Ensure parent directory exists for destination
116:         const parentDir = dirname(destPath);
117:         mkdirSync(parentDir, { recursive: true });
118:         
119:         if (isDirectory) {
120:           // Use cpSync with recursive and preserveTimestamps to properly copy .git
121:           cpSync(sourcePath, destPath, { 
122:             recursive: true, 
123:             preserveTimestamps: true,
124:             filter: () => true // Copy all files including hidden ones
125:           });
126:           // Verify copy succeeded before deleting source
127:           if (!existsSync(destPath)) {
128:             throw new Error(`Failed to copy directory from ${sourcePath} to ${destPath}`);
129:           }
130:           // Delete source directory recursively
131:           rmSync(sourcePath, { recursive: true, force: true });
132:         } else {
133:           // Use cpSync for files too to preserve permissions
134:           cpSync(sourcePath, destPath, { preserveTimestamps: true });
135:           if (!existsSync(destPath)) {
136:             throw new Error(`Failed to copy file from ${sourcePath} to ${destPath}`);
137:           }
138:           rmSync(sourcePath, { force: true });
139:         }
140:       } else {
141:         // Re-throw other errors
142:         throw error;
143:       }
144:     }
145:   }
146: 
147:   async checkFossilAvailable(): Promise<boolean> {
148:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "version"]);
149:     return result.success;
150:   }
151: 
152:   async getFossilVersion(): Promise<string | null> {
153:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "version"]);
154:     if (result.success) {
155:       const match = result.output.match(/(\d+\.\d+)/);
156:       return match ? match[1] : null;
157:     }
158:     return null;
159:   }

161:   async createFossilRepo(repoPath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
162:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "init", repoPath]);
163:     return {
164:       success: result.success,
165:       output: result.output,
166:       error: result.error || undefined,
167:     };
168:   }
169: 
170:   async createBranch(branchName: string, repoType: "git" | "fossil", upstreamPath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
171:     if (repoType === "git") {
172:       const result = await this.execCommand(
173:         ["git", "checkout", "-B", branchName],
174:         upstreamPath
175:       );
176:       return {
177:         success: result.success,
178:         output: result.output,
179:         error: result.error || undefined,
180:       };
181:     } else {
182:       const result = await this.execCommand(
183:         ["fossil", "branch", "new", branchName, "current"],
184:         upstreamPath
185:       );
186:       return {
187:         success: result.success,
188:         output: result.output,
189:         error: result.error || undefined,
190:       };
191:     }
192:   }
193: 
194:   async createFossilUser(
195:     repoPath: string,
196:     username: string,
197:     password: string
198:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
199:     // Create user with DEV capabilities (d - develop, i - check-in, o - check-out)
200:     const result = await this.execCommand([
201:       "fossil",
202:       "user",
203:       "new",
204:       username,
205:       username,
206:       password,
207:       "-R",
208:       repoPath,
209:     ]);
210: 
211:     if (result.success) {
212:       // Set capabilities to DEV (d=develop, i=check-in, o=check-out)
213:       const capResult = await this.execCommand([
214:         "fossil",
215:         "user",
216:         "capabilities",
217:         username,
218:         "dio",
219:         "-R",
220:         repoPath,
221:       ]);
222: 
223:       return {
224:         success: capResult.success,
225:         output: capResult.output,
226:         error: capResult.error || undefined,
227:       };
228:     }
229: 
230:     return {
231:       success: false,
232:       output: result.output,
233:       error: result.error || "Failed to create user",
234:     };
235:   }
236: 
237:   async openFossil(repoPath: string, workDir: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
238:     const result = await this.execCommand(
239:       ["fossil", "open", repoPath],
240:       workDir
241:     );
242:     return {
243:       success: result.success,
244:       output: result.output,
245:       error: result.error || undefined,
246:     };
247:   }
248: 
249:   async importGitToFossil(gitUrl: string, workDir: string, credential?: Credential): Promise<VCSResult> {
250:     let url = gitUrl;
251:     
252:     // Inject credentials if provided and HTTPS
253:     if (credential?.type === "https" && !this.isSshUrl(gitUrl)) {
254:       url = this.injectHttpsCredentials(gitUrl, credential);
255:     }
256: 
257:     try {
258:       new URL(url);
259:     } catch {
260:       // Allow SSH URLs
261:       if (!this.isSshUrl(url)) {
262:         return {
263:           success: false,
264:           error: "Invalid Git URL format",
265:         };
266:       }
267:     }
268: 
269:     // Create fossil repo first
270:     const fossilPath = `${workDir}/.fossil`;
271:     const initResult = await this.createFossilRepo(fossilPath);
272:     if (!initResult.success) {
273:       return initResult;
274:     }
275: 
276:     // Import from git
277:     const result = await this.execCommand(
278:       ["fossil", "import", "--git", url, fossilPath],
279:       workDir
280:     );
281: 
282:     if (result.success) {
283:       // Open the fossil repo in the workdir
284:       const openResult = await this.openFossil(fossilPath, workDir);
285:       return openResult;
286:     }
287: 
288:     return {
289:       success: false,
290:       output: result.output,
291:       error: result.error || "Failed to import from Git",
292:     };
293:   }
294: 
295:   async cloneFossil(
296:     sourcePath: string,
297:     targetDir: string
298:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
299:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
300:     const { dirname } = await import("path");
301: 
302:     // Ensure target directory exists
303:     try {
304:       mkdirSync(targetDir, { recursive: true });
305:     } catch {
306:       // Directory might already exist
307:     }
308: 
309:     // Clone the fossil repo
310:     const result = await this.execCommand([
311:       "fossil",
312:       "clone",
313:       sourcePath,
314:       `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
315:     ]);
316: 
317:     if (result.success) {
318:       // Open the cloned repo
319:       const openResult = await this.openFossil(
320:         `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
321:         targetDir
322:       );
323:       return openResult;
324:     }
325: 
326:     return {
327:       success: false,
328:       output: result.output,
329:       error: result.error || "Failed to clone Fossil repository",
330:     };
331:   }
332: 
333:   async sync(
334:     workDir: string,
335:     direction: "pull" | "push",
336:     credential?: Credential
337:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
338:     // Fossil sync doesn't support credentials directly
339:     // Credentials would need to be in the URL
340:     const command = direction === "pull" ? "pull" : "push";
341:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", command], workDir);
342: 
343:     return {
344:       success: result.success,
345:       output: result.output,
346:       error: result.error || undefined,
347:     };
348:   }

351:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "changes"], workDir);
352:     return {
353:       success: result.success,
354:       output: result.output,
355:       error: result.error || undefined,
356:     };
357:   }

361:       ["fossil", "commit", "-m", message],
362:       workDir
363:     );
364: 
365:     return {
366:       success: result.success,
367:       output: result.output,
368:       error: result.error || undefined,
369:     };

373:     const result = await this.execCommand(
374:       ["fossil", "timeline", "-n", limit.toString()],
375:       workDir
376:     );
377: 
378:     return {
379:       success: result.success,
380:       output: result.output,
381:       error: result.error || undefined,
382:     };
383:   }
384: 
385:   async cloneRepository(
386:     repoUrl: string,
387:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
388:     targetDir: string,
389:     credential?: Credential,
390:     sourceBranch?: string
391:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
392:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
393:     
394:     // Ensure target directory exists
395:     try {
396:       mkdirSync(targetDir, { recursive: true });
397:     } catch {
398:       // Directory might already exist
399:     }
400: 
401:     if (repoType === "git") {
402:       let url = repoUrl;
403:       let sshKeyPath: string | null = null;
404:       let env: Record<string, string> | undefined = undefined;
405: 
406:       // Handle credentials
407:       if (credential) {
408:         if (credential.type === "https" && !this.isSshUrl(repoUrl)) {
409:           url = this.injectHttpsCredentials(repoUrl, credential);
410:         } else if (credential.type === "ssh" && this.isSshUrl(repoUrl)) {
411:           // Create temp SSH key file
412:           sshKeyPath = this.createTempSshKeyFile(credential.privateKey);
413:           env = {
414:             GIT_SSH_COMMAND: this.buildGitSshCommand(sshKeyPath),
415:           };
416:         }
417:       }
418: 
419:       try {
420:         // Clone Git repository with optional branch
421:         const cloneArgs = sourceBranch 
422:           ? ["git", "clone", "--branch", sourceBranch, url, targetDir]
423:           : ["git", "clone", url, targetDir];
424:         const result = await this.execCommand(
425:           cloneArgs,
426:           targetDir,
427:           env
428:         );
429:         
430:         if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, credential?.type === "ssh" ? "ssh" : "https")) {
431:           return {
432:             success: false,
433:             output: result.output,
434:             error: credential?.type === "ssh" 
435:               ? "SSH authentication failed. Please check your private key and repository access."
436:               : "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
437:           };
438:         }
439:         
440:         if (result.success) {
441:           return {
442:             success: true,
443:             output: result.output,
444:           };
445:         }
446:         
447:         // If git clone failed but directory has content, try cloning into current directory
448:         const result2 = await this.execCommand(
449:           ["git", "clone", url, "."],
450:           targetDir,
451:           env
452:         );
453: 
454:         if (!result2.success && this.isAuthError(result2.error, credential?.type === "ssh" ? "ssh" : "https")) {
455:           return {
456:             success: false,
457:             output: result2.output,
458:             error: credential?.type === "ssh" 
459:               ? "SSH authentication failed. Please check your private key and repository access."
460:               : "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
461:           };
462:         }
463:         
464:         return {
465:           success: result2.success,
466:           output: result2.output,
467:           error: result2.error || undefined,
468:         };
469:       } finally {
470:         // Clean up temp SSH key file
471:         if (sshKeyPath) {
472:           this.deleteTempSshKeyFile(sshKeyPath);
473:         }
474:       }
475:     } else {
476:       // Clone Fossil repository - inject credentials if HTTPS
477:       let url = repoUrl;
478:       if (credential?.type === "https" && !this.isSshUrl(repoUrl)) {
479:         url = this.injectHttpsCredentials(repoUrl, credential);
480:       }
481: 
482:       const result = await this.execCommand(
483:         ["fossil", "clone", url, `${targetDir}/.fossil`],
484:         targetDir
485:       );
486:       
487:       if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, "https")) {
488:         return {
489:           success: false,
490:           output: result.output,
491:           error: "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
492:         };
493:       }
494:       
495:       if (result.success) {
496:         // Open the cloned repo in the target directory
497:         const openResult = await this.openFossil(
498:           `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
499:           targetDir
500:         );
501:         
502:         if (!openResult.success) {
503:           return openResult;
504:         }
505:         
506:         // If sourceBranch specified, checkout that branch
507:         if (sourceBranch) {
508:           const checkoutResult = await this.execCommand(
509:             ["fossil", "checkout", sourceBranch],
510:             targetDir
511:           );
512:           if (!checkoutResult.success) {
513:             return {
514:               success: false,
515:               output: checkoutResult.output,
516:               error: `Failed to checkout source branch '${sourceBranch}': ${checkoutResult.error}`,
517:             };
518:           }
519:         }
520:         
521:         return openResult;
522:       }
523:       
524:       return {
525:         success: false,
526:         output: result.output,
527:         error: result.error || "Failed to clone Fossil repository",
528:       };
529:     }
530:   }
531: 
532:   async importToFossil(
533:     upstreamPath: string,
534:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
535:     fossilPath: string
536:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
537:     if (repoType === "git") {
538:       // Create a fossil repo from the current working tree only (no git history).
539:       // This is faster than git fast-export --all and avoids issues with signed tags.
540: 
541:       // Step 1: Init the fossil repo
542:       const initResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "init", fossilPath]);
543:       if (!initResult.success) {
544:         return { success: false, error: `Fossil init failed: ${initResult.error}` };
545:       }
546: 
547:       // Step 2: Open it in the upstream working tree
548:       const openResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "open", fossilPath, "--nested", "--force"], upstreamPath);
549:       if (!openResult.success) {
550:         return { success: false, error: `Fossil open failed: ${openResult.error}` };
551:       }
552: 
553:       // Step 3: Add all files and commit the current state
554:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "addremove"], upstreamPath);
555:       if (!addResult.success) {
556:         return { success: false, error: `Fossil addremove failed: ${addResult.error}` };
557:       }
558: 
559:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
560:         ["fossil", "commit", "-m", "Initial import", "--no-warnings"],
561:         upstreamPath
562:       );
563: 
564:       return {
565:         success: commitResult.success,
566:         output: commitResult.output,
567:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
568:       };
569:     } else {
570:       // For fossil, clone from the upstream fossil repo
571:       const result = await this.execCommand(
572:         ["fossil", "clone", `${upstreamPath}/.fossil`, fossilPath],
573:         upstreamPath
574:       );
575:       
576:       return {
577:         success: result.success,
578:         output: result.output,
579:         error: result.error || undefined,
580:       };
581:     }
582:   }
583: 
584:   async openFossilCheckout(
585:     fossilPath: string,
586:     targetPath: string
587:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
588:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
589:     
590:     // Ensure target directory exists
591:     try {
592:       mkdirSync(targetPath, { recursive: true });
593:     } catch {
594:       // Directory might already exist
595:     }
596:     
597:     // Open the fossil repo in the target directory
598:     const result = await this.execCommand(
599:       ["fossil", "open", fossilPath],
600:       targetPath
601:     );
602:     
603:     return {
604:       success: result.success,
605:       output: result.output,
606:       error: result.error || undefined,
607:     };
608:   }
609: 
610:   async exportFromFossil(
611:     fossilPath: string,
612:     upstreamPath: string,
613:     repoType: "git" | "fossil"
614:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
615:     if (repoType === "git") {
616:       // Export from Fossil to Git upstream
617:       // Use fossil export to create a git-fast-export stream
618:       const result = await this.execCommand(
619:         ["fossil", "export", "--git", fossilPath],
620:         upstreamPath
621:       );
622:       
623:       if (result.success) {
624:         // Apply the export to git
625:         const applyResult = await this.execCommand(
626:           ["git", "fast-import"],
627:           upstreamPath
628:         );
629:         return {
630:           success: applyResult.success,
631:           output: applyResult.output,
632:           error: applyResult.error || undefined,
633:         };
634:       }
635:       
636:       return {
637:         success: false,
638:         output: result.output,
639:         error: result.error || undefined,
640:       };
641:     } else {
642:       // For fossil, push directly from checkout
643:       return {
644:         success: true,
645:         output: "Fossil repos sync directly",
646:       };
647:     }
648:   }
649: 
650:   async pushToRemote(
651:     upstreamPath: string,
652:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
653:     credential?: Credential,
654:     branch?: string
655:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
656:     if (repoType === "git") {
657:       let sshKeyPath: string | null = null;
658:       let env: Record<string, string> | undefined = undefined;
659: 
660:       // Handle SSH credentials
661:       if (credential?.type === "ssh") {
662:         sshKeyPath = this.createTempSshKeyFile(credential.privateKey);
663:         env = {
664:           GIT_SSH_COMMAND: this.buildGitSshCommand(sshKeyPath),
665:         };
666:       }
667: 
668:       try {
669:         const pushArgs = branch ? ["push", "origin", branch] : ["push", "origin"];
670:         const result = await this.execCommand(["git", ...pushArgs], upstreamPath, env);
671: 
672:         // Check if the failure is due to no upstream branch configured
673:         // This is expected in test environments or new repos without remotes
674:         if (!result.success && 
675:             (result.error?.includes("no upstream branch") || 
676:              result.error?.includes("has no upstream branch"))) {
677:           return {
678:             success: true,
679:             output: "No remote configured - skipping push",
680:           };
681:         }
682: 
683:         if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, "ssh")) {
684:           return {
685:             success: false,
686:             output: result.output,
687:             error: "SSH authentication failed. Please check your private key and repository access.",
688:           };
689:         }
690: 
691:         return {
692:           success: result.success,
693:           output: result.output,
694:           error: result.error || undefined,
695:         };
696:       } finally {
697:         if (sshKeyPath) {
698:           this.deleteTempSshKeyFile(sshKeyPath);
699:         }
700:       }
701:     } else {
702:       // Fossil push
703:       const args = branch ? ["push", branch] : ["push"];
704:       const result = await this.execCommand(
705:         ["fossil", ...args],
706:         upstreamPath
707:       );
708: 
709:       if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, "https")) {
710:         return {
711:           success: false,
712:           output: result.output,
713:           error: "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
714:         };
715:       }
716: 
717:       return {
718:         success: result.success,
719:         output: result.output,
720:         error: result.error || undefined,
721:       };
722:     }
723:   }
724: 
725:   async setupSessionWorktree(
726:     projectId: string,
727:     sessionId: string,
728:     worktreePath: string
729:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
730:     const { getProjectPath } = await import("../config/paths.js");
731:     const projectPath = getProjectPath(projectId);
732:     const fossilPath = `${projectPath}/repo.fossil`;
733: 
734:     // Ensure worktree directory exists
735:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
736:     try {
737:       mkdirSync(worktreePath, { recursive: true });
738:     } catch {
739:       // Directory might already exist
740:     }
741: 
742:     // Check if fossil repo exists
743:     const { existsSync } = await import("fs");
744:     if (!existsSync(fossilPath)) {
745:       return {
746:         success: false,
747:         error: "Project fossil repository not found",
748:       };
749:     }
750: 
751:     // Open the fossil repo in the worktree
752:     return await this.openFossil(fossilPath, worktreePath);
753:   }
754: 
755:   // New methods for commit flow
756: 
757:   async fossilUp(agentWorkspacePath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
758:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "up"], agentWorkspacePath);
759:     return {
760:       success: result.success,
761:       output: result.output,
762:       error: result.error || undefined,
763:     };
764:   }
765: 
766:   async cleanCopyToUpstream(
767:     agentWorkspacePath: string,
768:     upstreamPath: string
769:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
770:     const { readdirSync, statSync, copyFileSync, mkdirSync, unlinkSync, rmdirSync } = await import("fs");
771:     const { join, relative } = await import("path");
772: 
773:     const { existsSync: fsExistsSync } = await import("fs");
774:     
775:     try {
776:       // Step 1: Get list of files that SHOULD exist according to fossil
777:       // These are the files tracked in the current checkout
778:       const fossilTrackedFiles: Set<string> = new Set();
779:       const fossilLsResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "ls"], agentWorkspacePath);
780:       if (fossilLsResult.success && fossilLsResult.output) {
781:         const lines = fossilLsResult.output.split("\n").filter(line => line.trim());
782:         for (const line of lines) {
783:           fossilTrackedFiles.add(line.trim());
784:         }
785:       }
786: 
787:       // Step 2: Get list of tracked files in upstream (source of truth for deletions)
788:       const upstreamTrackedFiles: string[] = [];
789:       if (fsExistsSync(upstreamPath)) {
790:         const gitLsResult = await this.execCommand(["git", "ls-files"], upstreamPath);
791:         if (gitLsResult.success && gitLsResult.output) {
792:           const lines = gitLsResult.output.split("\n").filter(line => line.trim());
793:           upstreamTrackedFiles.push(...lines);
794:         }
795:       }
796: 
797:       // Step 3: Copy all files from agent-workspace to upstream
798:       // Exclude VCS metadata directories
799:       // Files on disk but NOT in fossil ls are either:
800:       // - Untracked files (should be copied)
801:       // - Deleted tracked files (should NOT be copied)
802:       const excludeItems = new Set([".git", ".fossil", ".fslckout"]);
803:       
804:       const copyRecursive = (source: string, dest: string, basePath: string = source) => {
805:         if (!fsExistsSync(source)) return;
806: 
807:         const entries = readdirSync(source, { withFileTypes: true });
808:         for (const entry of entries) {
809:           // Skip VCS metadata directories
810:           if (excludeItems.has(entry.name)) continue;
811: 
812:           const sourcePath = join(source, entry.name);
813:           const destPath = join(dest, entry.name);
814:           const relativePath = relative(basePath, sourcePath);
815: 
816:           if (entry.isDirectory()) {
817:             if (!fsExistsSync(destPath)) {
818:               mkdirSync(destPath, { recursive: true });
819:             }
820:             copyRecursive(sourcePath, destPath, basePath);
821:           } else {
822:             // Only copy if file should exist according to fossil,
823:             // OR if it's not tracked at all (new untracked file)
824:             const shouldCopy = fossilTrackedFiles.has(relativePath) || !upstreamTrackedFiles.includes(relativePath);
825:             if (shouldCopy) {
826:               copyFileSync(sourcePath, destPath);
827:             }
828:           }
829:         }
830:       };
831: 
832:       if (fsExistsSync(agentWorkspacePath)) {
833:         copyRecursive(agentWorkspacePath, upstreamPath, agentWorkspacePath);
834:       }
835: 
836:       // Step 4: Delete from upstream files that are:
837:       // - Tracked in upstream (from git ls-files)
838:       // - Either not on agent disk OR not tracked by fossil (meaning deleted)
839:       for (const trackedFile of upstreamTrackedFiles) {
840:         const agentFilePath = join(agentWorkspacePath, trackedFile);
841:         const upstreamFilePath = join(upstreamPath, trackedFile);
842:         
843:         // Delete if tracked in upstream but either:
844:         // 1. Not present on agent disk, OR
845:         // 2. Present on disk but NOT tracked by fossil (was deleted via fossil rm)
846:         const existsOnDisk = fsExistsSync(agentFilePath);
847:         const trackedByFossil = fossilTrackedFiles.has(trackedFile);
848:         const shouldDelete = !existsOnDisk || !trackedByFossil;
849:         
850:         if (shouldDelete && fsExistsSync(upstreamFilePath)) {
851:           unlinkSync(upstreamFilePath);
852:           
853:           // Clean up empty parent directories
854:           let parentDir = join(upstreamPath, trackedFile);
855:           while (true) {
856:             parentDir = join(parentDir, "..");
857:             const resolvedParent = join(parentDir); // Normalize
858:             if (resolvedParent === upstreamPath) break;
859:             
860:             try {
861:               const entries = readdirSync(resolvedParent);
862:               if (entries.length === 0) {
863:                 rmdirSync(resolvedParent);
864:               } else {
865:                 break;
866:               }
867:             } catch {
868:               break;
869:             }
870:           }
871:         }
872:       }
873: 
874:       return {
875:         success: true,
876:         output: "Files copied successfully",
877:       };
878:     } catch (error) {
879:       return {
880:         success: false,
881:         error: `Failed to copy files: ${error}`,
882:       };
883:     }
884:   }
885: 
886:   async commitUpstream(
887:     upstreamPath: string,
888:     repoType: "git" | "fossil"
889:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
890:     const message = `Mimo commit at ${new Date().toISOString()}`;
891: 
892:     if (repoType === "git") {
893:       // Git: add all and commit
894:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["git", "add", "-A"], upstreamPath);
895:       if (!addResult.success) {
896:         return {
897:           success: false,
898:           output: addResult.output,
899:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
900:         };
901:       }
902: 
903:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
904:         ["git", "commit", "-m", message],
905:         upstreamPath
906:       );
907: 
908:       // Check if nothing to commit
909:       if (commitResult.error?.includes("nothing to commit") || 
910:           commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit")) {
911:         return {
912:           success: true,
913:           output: "No changes to commit",
914:         };
915:       }
916: 
917:       return {
918:         success: commitResult.success,
919:         output: commitResult.output,
920:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
921:       };
922:     } else {
923:       // Fossil: addremove and commit
924:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "addremove"], upstreamPath);
925:       if (!addResult.success) {
926:         return {
927:           success: false,
928:           output: addResult.output,
929:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
930:         };
931:       }
932: 
933:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
934:         ["fossil", "commit", "-m", message],
935:         upstreamPath
936:       );
937: 
938:       return {
939:         success: commitResult.success,
940:         output: commitResult.output,
941:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
942:       };
943:     }
944:   }
945: 
946:   async pushUpstream(
947:     upstreamPath: string,
948:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
949:     credential?: Credential,
950:     branch?: string
951:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
952:     if (repoType === "git") {
953:       let sshKeyPath: string | null = null;
954:       let env: Record<string, string> | undefined = undefined;
955: 
956:       // Handle SSH credentials
957:       if (credential?.type === "ssh") {
958:         sshKeyPath = this.createTempSshKeyFile(credential.privateKey);
959:         env = {
960:           GIT_SSH_COMMAND: this.buildGitSshCommand(sshKeyPath),
961:         };
962:       }
963: 
964:       try {
965:         const pushArgs = branch ? ["push", "origin", branch] : ["push", "origin"];
966:         const result = await this.execCommand(["git", ...pushArgs], upstreamPath, env);
967: 
968:         // Check if the failure is due to no upstream branch configured
969:         // This is expected in test environments or new repos without remotes
970:         if (!result.success && 
971:             (result.error?.includes("no upstream branch") || 
972:              result.error?.includes("has no upstream branch"))) {
973:           return {
974:             success: true,
975:             output: "No remote configured - skipping push",
976:           };
977:         }
978: 
979:         if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, credential?.type === "ssh" ? "ssh" : "https")) {
980:           return {
981:             success: false,
982:             output: result.output,
983:             error: credential?.type === "ssh" 
984:               ? "SSH authentication failed. Please check your private key and repository access."
985:               : "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
986:           };
987:         }
988: 
989:         return {
990:           success: result.success,
991:           output: result.output,
992:           error: result.error || undefined,
993:         };
994:       } finally {
995:         if (sshKeyPath) {
996:           this.deleteTempSshKeyFile(sshKeyPath);
997:         }
998:       }
999:     } else {
1000:       const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "push"], upstreamPath);
1001: 
1002:       if (!result.success && this.isAuthError(result.error, "https")) {
1003:         return {
1004:           success: false,
1005:           output: result.output,
1006:           error: "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access.",
1007:         };
1008:       }
1009: 
1010:       return {
1011:         success: result.success,
1012:         output: result.output,
1013:         error: result.error || undefined,
1014:       };
1015:     }
1016:   }
1017: }
1018:

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:22:56)

Now I understand the context. The current implementation uses `cleanCopyToUpstream` which:
1. Gets files tracked by fossil
2. Gets files tracked by git upstream
3. Does a manual recursive copy
4. Deletes files from upstream that were deleted in fossil

The user wants to change this to use `fossil diff --from ... --to ...` instead.

Let me visualize what the user wants:

**Current Flow:**
```
agent-workspace ──fossil──> repo.fossil
       │
       │ cleanCopyToUpstream
       │ (manual file copying)
       ▼
   upstream (git)
```

**Proposed Flow:**
```
agent-workspace ──fossil──> repo.fossil
       │
       │ fossil diff --from A --to B -v --internal
       │ (generates patch)
       ▼
   upstream (git)
```

The user wants to use `fossil diff --from <first_commit> --to <last_commit> -v --internal` to generate a patch that can be applied to the upstream.

Let me think about this:

1. `fossil timeline -n 0` shows all commits
2. First commit = from
3. Last commit = to
4. `fossil diff --from <first> --to <last> -v --internal` generates a patch

But wait... there are some questions here:

1. How does this patch get applied to the git upstream? The upstream is git, not fossil.
2. The `-v` flag in fossil diff shows verbose output, `--internal` shows internal delta format
3. Is this meant to be applied as a git patch? If so, is the format compatible?

Let me think about the workflow more carefully:

**Current Commit Flow:**
1. Agent works in agent-workspace (fossil checkout)
2. Agent commits to fossil (repo.fossil)
3. When user clicks "Commit", it:
   - Syncs agent-workspace with repo.fossil (`fossil up`)


4. Copies files from agent-workspace to upstream (`cleanCopyToUpstream`)
5. Commits in upstream (git)

**Proposed Flow:**
1. Agent works in agent-workspace (fossil checkout)
2. Agent commits to fossil (repo.fossil)
3. When user clicks "Commit":
   - Generate a patch from fossil commits: `fossil diff --from FIRST --to LAST -v --internal`
   - Apply that patch to upstream somehow
   - Commit in upstream

The critical challenge is patch compatibility between fossil and git. The internal delta format might not translate directly to git's patching mechanism. I'll need to investigate how to bridge this gap between version control systems.

Fossil's internal delta format is fundamentally different from git's standard diff. Using `--unified` could potentially provide a more compatible patch format that git might recognize. However, the core complexity lies in file synchronization - managing new files, deletions, and ensuring the patch applies cleanly across different version control systems.

The key considerations are patch generation, file tracking, and maintaining the integrity of the repository's state during the cross-VCS transfer process. The `--from` and `--to` parameters define the precise range of changes to capture, which allows selective commit transfer between repositories.

The command suggests generating a patch between specific fossil commits, with the `-v` and `--internal` flags indicating verbose output and internal delta format. However, applying this patch to a Git repository presents significant compatibility challenges due to fundamental differences in version control system implementations.

Exploring alternative strategies like `git fast-import` or investigating Fossil's native export capabilities might provide a more robust solution for transferring changes between these distinct version control systems.

The patch generation workflow seems straightforward: identify the commit range using `fossil timeline`, then generate a patch between those commits. The key steps involve extracting the first and last commit hashes and using them to create a comprehensive diff.

However, the actual implementation would require careful handling of patch format compatibility, especially when bridging Fossil and Git repositories. The user hints at an existing mechanism for patch application that isn't immediately clear.

I'll need to investigate the precise method for applying the generated patch to the upstream Git repository, ensuring the `--internal` flag doesn't introduce unexpected complexity in the transfer process.

**Your Proposed Flow:**
```
┌─────────────────┐     fossil timeline    ┌────────────────┐
│  agent-workspace│◄──────────────────────►│  repo.fossil   │
│   (checkout)    │                        │   (history)    │
└────────┬────────┘                        └────────────────┘
         │                                        
         │ fossil diff --from A --to B     
         │ -v --internal                   
         ▼                                        
┌─────────────────┐      apply patch       ┌─────────────┐
│    upstream     │◄──────────────────────►│   remote    │
│   (git repo)    │                        │   (origin)  │
└─────────────────┘                        └─────────────┘
```

**Questions that come up:**

1. **Patch format compatibility** - `fossil diff --internal` produces fossil's internal delta format. Does git understand this? Or would you need `--unified` for a universal diff format?

2. **Applying to git** - Once you have the fossil patch, how do you apply it to the git upstream? Are you thinking:
   - `git apply` (if unified format)
   - `patch` command
   - Some other mechanism?

3. **File lifecycle** - The current logic handles file deletion (files removed via `fossil rm`). Does the patch approach naturally handle deletions, or would you need extra logic?

4. **Edge cases** - What about:
   - Binary files?
   - File permission changes?
   - Rename detection?

**The commit range approach:**
```
$ fossil timeline -n 0
=== 2026-04-09 ===
02:30:04 [abcdef] First commit message
02:45:12 [123456] Second commit message
...
03:15:00 [xyz789] Latest commit

from = abcdef (first)
to   = xyz789 (last)

$ fossil diff --from abcdef --to xyz789 -v --internal
```

This would capture ALL changes across the session. But I'm curious - **how do you envision applying this patch to the git upstream?** The format matters for interoperability.

Also, is this primarily about:
- **Simplicity** (one patch vs manual file operations)?
- **Accuracy** (capturing exact fossil changes)?
- **Performance** (faster than recursive copy)?
- **Atomicity** (single operation vs many file ops)?

What's driving this change?

## User (2026-04-09 02:25:11)

ok, what about using 'fossil git export' to a temporary directory, then from the git generate the diffs and then use these diff to apply to the upstream git/fossil?

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:25:17)

Interesting! The user is proposing a different approach:

1. `fossil git export` to a temporary directory (this exports fossil history as a git-fast-export stream)
2. From the temp directory (which would be a git repo), generate the diffs
3. Apply those diffs to the upstream git/fossil

This is clever because it leverages Fossil's built-in git export capability and then uses standard git tools to generate the patch, which can be applied to git upstream.

Let me think through this:

```
┌─────────────────┐     fossil git export    ┌─────────────────────┐
│  agent-workspace│────────────────────────►│  temp-git-repo/     │
│   (checkout)    │    (fast-export stream)   │  (git clone)        │
└────────┬────────┘                         └──────────┬──────────┘
         │                                              │
         │                                              │ git diff A..B
         │                                              ▼
         │                                    ┌─────────────────────┐
         │                                    │  patch file         │
         │                                    │  (unified diff)      │
         │                                    └──────────┬──────────┘
         │                                               │

**Key insight**: `fossil git export` outputs a **git-fast-export** stream that can be imported into git using `git fast-import`. This bridges the format gap elegantly.

Let me think through the mechanics...

**The sequence would be:**

1. **Initial state** - At session start, export fossil to temp-git as baseline
2. **At commit time**:
   - Re-export fossil to temp-git (now with new changes)
   - Generate diff: `git diff baseline-commit..latest-commit`
   - Apply to upstream: `git apply` or `git am`

**But I have questions:**

**1. Baseline management** - Do you need to track what was already exported? Or does `fossil git export` always export the full history, and you just take the latest commit?

```
# Does this export just new commits, or everything?
fossil git export repo.fossil | git fast-import
```

**2. Commit identification** - How do you know which commits in temp-git correspond to "new changes" vs "already synced"?

```
# In temp-git, what are the FROM and TO commits?
git diff <from>..<to> > patch
```

**3. Fossil upstream case** - If upstream is fossil, can you apply a git-formatted patch? Fossil understands unified diff but not all git extensions.

**4. What's the actual advantage?** - Compared to the current manual copy approach, this seems more complex. What problem are you solving?
- **Exact change tracking** (patch knows what changed vs manual copy)?
- **Performance** (incremental vs full copy)?
- **Metadata preservation** (permissions, renames)?
- **Atomicity**?

The current approach copies files file-by-file. The patch approach is more "transactional" - you get one coherent changeset.

**Actually, I just realized something:**

With `fossil git export`, you might not even need the intermediate patch step. You could:

```
1. fossil git export repo.fossil > export.stream
2. cd upstream && git fast-import < export.stream
3. git reset --hard HEAD  # or whatever to sync working tree
```

But this would **overwrite** upstream's git history with fossil's. That's probably not what you want.

**Real question**: Are you trying to:
- **Sync working tree contents** (what files look like now)?
- **Sync commit history** (preserve fossil commits in git)?

Because those are two very different problems. The current code does (1). Your proposal with patches does a version of (1) with more precision. But `fossil git export` is really designed for (2) - full history migration.

What are you actually after?

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│       │ 1. Identify commit range                            │
│       │    first = oldest commit in session                 │
│       │    last  = newest commit in session               │
│       │                                                     │
│       ▼                                                     │
│  ┌────────────┐    2. Generate unified diff                   │
│  │ fossil diff│ ──────────────────────────► patch file       │
│  │ --from X  │    (works with both VCS)                     │
│  │ --to Y    │                                             │
│  └────────────┘                                             │
│       │                                                     │
│       │ 3. Apply patch                                       │
│       ▼                                                     │
│  ┌─────────────┐      ┌─────────────┐                       │
│  │   git       │      │   fossil    │                       │
│  │   apply     │ OR   │   patch     │                       │
│  │   -p1       │      │   (builtin) │                       │
│  └─────────────┘      └─────────────┘                       │
│       upstream/                                             │
│                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**The key insight**: Fossil's unified diff format is **universal**. Both `git apply` and `fossil patch` can consume it.

**But here's the critical question:**

```
fossil timeline -n 0
===

2026-04-09 [a1b2c3] Initial session commit
2026-04-09 [d4e5f6] Added feature X
2026-04-09 [g7h8i9] Fixed bug Y   <-- current checkout
```

When generating the patch:
- **From** = a1b2c3 (first commit of session)?
- **To** = g7h8i9 (current checkout)?

**But what if** the upstream already has some of these changes? You need to know **where to start**.

**Option A: Track "last synced" commit**
- Store the last commit hash that was synced to upstream
- Generate patch from that point to now
- Update after successful apply

**Option B: Full diff every time**
- Generate patch from session-start commit to now
- Apply to upstream (git/fossil will handle duplicates)

**Option C: Compare file states**
- Use `fossil diff` without --from/--to (shows current uncommitted changes)
- But this misses committed changes...

Which approach fits your mental model? Do you want:
1. **Incremental** (just new commits since last sync)?
2. **Full** (all session commits every time)?
3. **Uncommitted only** (just working tree changes)?

Also - does the patch need to include **commit metadata** (author, message, timestamp) or just **file changes**?

The `fossil diff` approach only gets file changes. If you want to preserve commit history in the upstream, that's a different problem...

**This requires tracking `LAST_SYNC`** - the last commit that was successfully applied to upstream.

**Critical question: Where do you store `LAST_SYNC`?**

Option A: **Session database**
```typescript
// Add to session record
interface Session {
  // ... existing fields
  lastSyncedCommit?: string;  // fossil commit hash
}
```

Option B: **Fossil tag** (inside the repo itself)
```bash
fossil tag add last-synced-to-upstream ghi789
```

Option C: **File in session directory**
```bash
echo "ghi789" > .mimo-last-synced
```

Option D: **Compare with upstream directly**
```bash
### Instead of tracking, compare fossil vs upstream file states
```

**Also need to consider: What if upstream has changed?**

If someone pushes to upstream between your syncs, the patch might not apply cleanly. Do you:
- Detect this and warn?
- Force push (overwrite)?
- Pull/merge first?

**And for the patch format itself**, since you want both git and fossil upstreams:

```bash
# Unified diff works for both
fossil diff --from $LAST_SYNC --to $CURRENT

### Apply to git
git apply patch.diff

# Apply to fossil  
fossil patch apply patch.diff
# OR (if fossil doesn't have patch command):
### apply with system patch command
```

**Questions:**

1. **Where should `LAST_SYNC` be stored?** My gut says session database (Option A) - it's explicit, queryable, survives repo operations.

2. **What happens if patch application fails?** (conflicts, upstream changed) - Rollback `LAST_SYNC`? Leave it as-is?

3. **Do you need atomic "all or nothing" patches?** If patch 1-5 has conflicts in commit 5, do you:
   - Apply 1-4 and skip 5?
   - Apply nothing and tell user to fix?

4. **For binary files** - unified diff doesn't handle binaries well. Fossil has `--binary` flag. Is that needed?

What's your preference on these?

Fossil: Help: diff





  FossilHelp: diff
  
    Login

  


  &#9776;Home
Timeline

Topic-List


The "diff" command:

Usage: fossil diff|gdiff ?OPTIONS? ?FILE1? ?FILE2 ...?

 Show the difference between the current version of each of the FILEs
specified (as they exist on disk) and that same file as it was checked-
out.  Or if the FILE arguments are omitted, show all unsaved changes
currently in the working check-out.  The "gdiff" variant means to
use a GUI diff.

 The default output format is a "unified patch" (the same as the
output of "diff -u" on most unix systems).  Many alternative formats
are available.  A few of the more useful alternatives:


 --tk            Pop up a Tcl/Tk-based GUI to show the diff
 --by            Show a side-by-side diff in the default web browser
 -b              Show a linear diff in the default web browser
 -y              Show a text side-by-side diff
 --webpage       Format output as HTML
 --webpage -y    HTML output in the side-by-side format

 The "--from VERSION" option is used to specify the source check-in
for the diff operation.  If not specified, the source check-in is the
base check-in for the current check-out. Similarly, the "--to VERSION"
option specifies the check-in from which the second version of the file
or files is taken.  If there is no "--to" option then the (possibly edited)
files in the current check-out are used.  The "--checkin VERSION" option
shows the changes made by check-in VERSION relative to its primary parent.
The "--branch BRANCHNAME" shows all the changes on the branch BRANCHNAME.

 With the "--from VERSION" option, if VERSION is actually a directory name
(not a tag or check-in hash) then the files under that directory are used
as the baseline for the diff.

 The "-i" command-line option forces the use of Fossil's own internal
diff logic rather than any external diff program that might be configured
using the "setting" command.  If no external diff program is configured,
then the "-i" option is a no-op.  The "-i" option converts "gdiff" into
"diff".

 The "--diff-binary" option enables or disables the inclusion of binary files
when using an external diff program.

 The "--binary" option causes files matching the glob PATTERN to be treated
as binary when considering if they should be used with the external diff
program.  This option overrides the "binary-glob" setting.

 These commands show differences between managed files. Use the "fossil xdiff"
command to see differences in unmanaged files.

 Options:

 --binary PATTERN          Treat files that match the glob PATTERN
as binary
 --branch BRANCH           Show diff of all changes on BRANCH
 --brief                   Show filenames only
 -b|--browser              Show the diff output in a web-browser
 --by                      Shorthand for "--browser -y"
 -ci|--checkin VERSION     Show diff of all changes in VERSION
 --command PROG            External diff program. Overrides "diff-command"
 -c|--context N            Show N lines of context around each change,
with negative N meaning show all content
 --dark                    Use dark mode for the Tcl/Tk-based GUI and HTML
 --diff-binary BOOL        Include binary files with external commands
 --exec-abs-paths          Force absolute path names on external commands
 --exec-rel-paths          Force relative path names on external commands
 -r|--from VERSION         Use VERSION as the baseline for the diff, or
if VERSION is a directory name, use files in
that directory as the baseline.
 -w|--ignore-all-space     Ignore white space when comparing lines
 -i|--internal             Use internal diff logic
 --invert                  Invert the diff
 --json                    Output formatted as JSON
 -n|--linenum              Show line numbers
 -N|--new-file             Alias for --verbose
 -s|--numstat              Show the number of added and deleted lines per
file, omitting the diff. When combined
with --brief, show only the total row.
 -y|--side-by-side         Side-by-side diff
 --strip-trailing-cr       Strip trailing CR
 --tcl                     Tcl-formatted output used internally by --tk
 --tclsh PATH              Tcl/Tk shell used for --tk (default: "tclsh")
 --tk                      Launch a Tcl/Tk GUI for display
 --to VERSION              Select VERSION as target for the diff
 --undo                    Use the undo buffer as the baseline
 --unified                 Unified diff
 -v|--verbose              Output complete text of added or deleted files
 -h|--versions             Show compared versions in the diff header
 --webpage                 Format output as a stand-alone HTML webpage
 -W|--width N              Width of lines in side-by-side diff
 -Z|--ignore-trailing-spaceIgnore changes to end-of-line whitespace





This page was generated in about
0.005s by
Fossil 2.29 [0201a1e2cc] 2026-04-07 09:58:25
```

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:32:20)

Interesting! The fossil diff output is NOT standard unified diff format. It has:
- "Index:" header (not standard)
- "==================================================================" separator (non-standard)
- "ADDED   file2.txt" annotation (non-standard)

Standard unified diff would look like:
```
--- file1.txt
+++ file1.txt
@@ -1,1 +1,3 @@
 Initial line
+Second line
+Third line
```

Let me check if fossil has an option to produce strict unified diff format, or if we need to transform it.

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:32:36)

<think> I see! The `-v` flag shows the full content for added files (showing `/dev/null` as source). This is the **standard unified diff format** that git understands.

### Tool Call [completed]: Test applying fossil patch to git

**Tool:** other
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:32:43
**Description:** Test applying fossil patch to git
**Command:** cd /tmp/fossil-git-patch-test

git add file1.txt

parent:       58670fd41b858978fa2a08859df4f9bddb6595b3 2026-04-08 23:31:50 UTC
child:        14d9cca48e9351ac6280777173108bbf43a8cd0e 2026-04-08 23:31:51 UTC
tags:         trunk
comment:      First commit (user: test)

=== File contents after checkout ===
Initial line
file2.txt does not exist (correctly removed)

=== Checking if fossil has 'patch' command ===
Usage: fossil patch SUBCOMMAND ?ARGS ..?

This command is used to create, view, and apply Fossil binary patches.
A Fossil binary patch is a single (binary) file that captures all of the
uncommitted changes of a check-out.  Use Fossil binary patches to transfer
proposed or incomplete changes between machines for testing or analysis.

  fossil patch alias add|rm|ls|list ?ARGS?

      Manage remote-name aliases, which act as short-form
      equivalents to REMOTE-CHECKOUT strings. Aliases are local to
      a given repository and do not sync. Subcommands:

        ... add ALIAS REMOTE-CHECKOUT       Add ALIAS as an alias
                                            for REMOTE-CHECKOUT.
        ... ls|list                         List all local aliases.
        ... rm ALIAS [ALIAS...]             Remove named aliases
        ... rm --all                        Remove all aliases

  fossil patch create [DIRECTORY] PATCHFILE

      Create a new binary patch in PATCHFILE that captures all uncommitted
      changes in the check-out at DIRECTORY, or the current directory if
      DIRECTORY is omitted.  If PATCHFILE is "-" then the binary patch
      is written to standard output.

      Options:
          -f|--force     Overwrite an existing patch with the same name

  fossil patch apply [DIRECTORY] PATCHFILE

      Apply the changes in PATCHFILE to the check-out at DIRECTORY, or
      in the current directory if DIRECTORY is omitted.

      Options:
          -f|--force     Apply the patch even though there are unsaved
                         changes in the current check-out.  Unsaved changes
                         are reverted and permanently lost.
          -n|--dry-run   Do nothing, but print what would have happened
          -v|--verbose   Extra output explaining what happens

  fossil patch diff [DIRECTORY] PATCHFILE
  fossil patch gdiff [DIRECTORY] PATCHFILE

      Show a human-readable diff for the patch in PATCHFILE and associated
      with the repository checked out in DIRECTORY.  The current
      directory is used if DIRECTORY is omitted. All the usual
      diff flags described at "fossil help diff" apply. With gdiff,
      gdiff-command is used instead of internal diff logic.  In addition:

          -f|--force     Continue trying to perform the diff even if
                         baseline information is missing from the current
                         repository

  fossil patch push REMOTE-CHECKOUT

      Create a patch for the current check-out, transfer that patch to
      a remote machine (using ssh) and apply the patch there.  The
      REMOTE-CHECKOUT is in one of the following formats:

          *   DIRECTORY
          *   HOST:DIRECTORY
          *   USER@HOST:DIRECTORY

      The name of the fossil executable on the remote host is specified
      by the --fossilcmd option, or if there is no --fossilcmd, it first
      tries "$HOME/bin/fossil" and if not found there it searches for any
      executable named "fossil" on the default $PATH set by SSH on the
      remote.

      Command-line options:

          -f|--force         Apply the patch even though there are unsaved
                             changes in the current check-out.  Unsaved
                             changes will be reverted and then the patch is
                             applied.
          --fossilcmd EXE    Name of the "fossil" executable on the remote
          -n|--dry-run       Do nothing, but print what would have happened
          -v|--verbose       Extra output explaining what happens


  fossil patch pull REMOTE-CHECKOUT

      Like "fossil patch push" except that the transfer is from remote
      to local.  All the same command-line options apply.

  fossil patch view PATCHFILE

      View a summary of the changes in the binary patch in PATCHFILE.
      Use "fossil patch diff" for detailed patch content.

          -v|--verbose       Show extra detail about the patch

=== Using system patch command instead ===
Usage: patch [OPTION]... [ORIGFILE [PATCHFILE]]

Input options:

  -p NUM  --strip=NUM  Strip NUM leading components from file names.
```
## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:33:26)

So fossil has its own `fossil patch` command that creates **binary patches**, not unified diff patches. These are fossil-specific and won't work with git.

However, fossil can still accept unified diff patches through the standard `patch` command.

Let me test applying the unified diff to fossil using the system `patch` command.

### Tool Call [completed]: Test applying unified diff to fossil with system patch

**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:33:31

echo "Current state (at first commit):"
cat file1.txt
ls -la file2.txt 2>/dev/null || echo "file2.txt: does not exist"

echo ""

patch -p0 -d fossil-workspace < patch-verbose.diff

echo ""

echo "file1.txt:"

echo ""

cat file2.txt

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:34:09)

## Summary

**Good news**: The unified diff format from fossil **DOES work** with both git and fossil upstreams!

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              PATCH FLOW - CONFIRMED WORKING                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  Agent Workspace (Fossil)                                       │
│       │                                                        │
│       │ fossil diff --from $LAST_SYNC --to $CURRENT -v        │
│       ▼                                                        │
│  ┌─────────────┐                                              │
│  │ unified     │  ← This format is standard/universal        │
│  │ diff patch  │                                              │
│  └──────┬──────┘                                              │
│         │                                                      │
│         ├────────────────┬────────────────┐                   │
│         │                │                │                   │
│         ▼                ▼                │                   │
│    ┌─────────┐    ┌──────────┐          │                   │
│    │ Git     │    │ Fossil   │          │                   │
│    │ apply   │    │ (system) │          │                   │
│    │patch.diff│    │patch -p0 │          │                   │
│    └────┬────┘    └────┬─────┘          │                   │
│         │              │                   │                   │
│         ▼              ▼                   │                   │
│    ┌─────────┐    ┌──────────┐            │                   │
│    │ Upstream│    │ Upstream │            │                   │
│    │ (git)   │    │ (fossil) │◄───────────┘                   │
│    └─────────┘    └──────────┘  fossil diff + patch          │
│                                                                 │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Key findings:**

1. **Unified diff (`-v` flag)** includes complete file content for new files (not just `ADDED filename`)
2. **Git accepts the patch** with `git apply`
3. **Fossil accepts the patch** with system `patch -p0` command
4. **The format is standard** - `Index:`, `---`, `+++`, `@@` markers

**Application commands:**
```bash
### For Git upstream
git apply patch.diff

# For Fossil upstream  
patch -p0 < patch.diff
### OR if fossil checkout is in different location:
patch -p0 -d /path/to/fossil/checkout < patch.diff
```

**Open questions still:**
1. Where to store `LAST_SYNC` commit hash?
2. What about binary files? (need `--binary` flag?)
3. How to handle file deletions in the patch?

Want me to test binary files and deletions next, or are you ready to start implementing this approach?## User (2026-04-09 02:34:19)

retry

echo "║  Commands:                                                            ║"
echo "║                                                                       ║"
echo "║  Generate:                                                            ║"
echo "║    fossil diff --from \$FIRST_COMMIT --to \$LAST_COMMIT -v             ║"
echo "║                                                                       ║"
echo "║  Apply to Git:                                                        ║"
echo "║    git apply patch.diff                                               ║"
echo "║                                                                       ║"
echo "║  Apply to Fossil:                                                     ║"
echo "║    patch -p0 < patch.diff                                             ║"
echo "║    OR use fossil's builtin patch:                                     ║"
echo "║    fossil patch apply patch.diff                                      ║"
echo "║                                                                       ║"
echo "║  Tested Operations:                                                   ║"
echo "║    ✓ File modifications                                               ║"
echo "║    ✓ File additions                                                   ║"
echo "║    ? File deletions (need to verify format)                           ║"
echo "║                                                                       ║"
echo "╚═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝"

```
╔═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                    FINAL PATCH COMPATIBILITY RESULTS                    ║
╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
║                                                                       ║
║  ✓ VERIFIED: Fossil unified diff works with BOTH Git and Fossil        ║
║                                                                       ║
╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
║                                                                       ║
║  WORKFLOW:                                                            ║
║                                                                       ║
║  ┌──────────────────┐    fossil diff --from X --to Y -v               ║
║  │ agent-workspace  │ ───────────────────────────────────► Patch File   ║
║  │ (fossil)         │                                              ║
║  └──────────────────┘                                               ║
║           │                                                           ║
║           │                                                           ║
║           ▼                                                           ║
║  ┌──────────────────┐    ┌──────────────────┐                         ║
║  │ Apply to Git     │    │ Apply to Fossil  │                         ║
║  │ git apply        │    │ patch -p0        │                         ║
║  └──────────────────┘    └──────────────────┘                         ║
║                                                                       ║
╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
║                                                                       ║

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:36:19)

<think> The tests confirm that the patch approach works. The unified diff format from fossil is compatible with both git and fossil (via system patch command).

Now, should I create a new OpenSpec change for implementing this feature?
## Agent (2026-04-09 02:36:20)

**✓ VERIFIED: The unified diff from Fossil works with both Git and Fossil.**

```
╔════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                    PATCH COMPATIBILITY CONFIRMED                    ║
╠════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
║                                                                    ║
║  ✓ Git:     git apply patch.diff           → WORKS                ║
║  ✓ Fossil:  patch -p0 < patch.diff         → WORKS                ║
║                                                                    ║
║  Command:   fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v                  ║
║  Format:    Unified diff (universal standard)                       ║
║                                                                    ║
╚════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
```

**What this means for your use case:**

```bash
# At session start - track first commit
FIRST_COMMIT=$(fossil timeline -n 0 | tail -1 | awk '{print $2}' | tr -d '[]')

### Work, commit, work, commit...

### At sync time - get last commit
LAST_COMMIT=$(fossil timeline -n 0 | head -3 | grep -v "===" | head -1 | awk '{print $2}' | tr -d '[]')

# Generate patch
fossil diff --from $FIRST_COMMIT --to $LAST_COMMIT -v > session.patch

### Apply to upstream (works for both git and fossil):
#   Git upstream:     cd upstream && git apply session.patch
#   Fossil upstream: cd upstream && patch -p0 < session.patch
```

**Important considerations:**

1. **Store `LAST_SYNC` commit** in session database so you know where to start next time
2. **File deletions** - need to verify the format, but unified diff supports them
3. **Binary files** - unified diff doesn't handle binaries well; may need `--binary` flag or separate handling

**Ready to implement this?** Want me to create an OpenSpec change with the design and tasks?

## User (2026-04-09 02:37:00)

nice, i want also to store every patch is generate in a folder
