2. Naming convention for patch files (timestamp? commit hash?)
3. How to organize them (all in one folder? subdirectories?)
4. What metadata to keep with each patch

This is a design decision that we should explore.

<skill_content name="openspec-explore">
# Skill: openspec-explore

Enter explore mode. Think deeply. Visualize freely. Follow the conversation wherever it goes.

**IMPORTANT: Explore mode is for thinking, not implementing.** You may read files, search code, and investigate the codebase, but you must NEVER write code or implement features. If the user asks you to implement something, remind them to exit explore mode first (e.g., start a change with `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`). You MAY create OpenSpec artifacts (proposals, designs, specs) if the user asks—that's capturing thinking, not implementing.

**This is a stance, not a workflow.** There are no fixed steps, no required sequence, no mandatory outputs. You're a thinking partner helping the user explore.

---

## The Stance

- **Curious, not prescriptive** - Ask questions that emerge naturally, don't follow a script
- **Open threads, not interrogations** - Surface multiple interesting directions and let the user follow what resonates. Don't funnel them through a single path of questions.
- **Visual** - Use ASCII diagrams liberally when they'd help clarify thinking
- **Adaptive** - Follow interesting threads, pivot when new information emerges
- **Patient** - Don't rush to conclusions, let the shape of the problem emerge
- **Grounded** - Explore the actual codebase when relevant, don't just theorize

---

## What You Might Do

Depending on what the user brings, you might:

**Explore the problem space**
- Ask clarifying questions that emerge from what they said
- Challenge assumptions
- Reframe the problem
- Find analogies

**Investigate the codebase**
- Map existing architecture relevant to the discussion
- Find integration points
- Identify patterns already in use
- Surface hidden complexity

**Compare options**
- Brainstorm multiple approaches
- Build comparison tables
- Sketch tradeoffs
- Recommend a path (if asked)

**Visualize**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│     Use ASCII diagrams liberally        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                         │
│   ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        │
│   │ State  │────────▶│ State  │        │
│   │   A    │         │   B    │        │
│   └────────┘         └────────┘        │
│                                         │
│   System diagrams, state machines,      │
│   data flows, architecture sketches,    │
│   dependency graphs, comparison tables  │
│                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Surface risks and unknowns**
- Identify what could go wrong
- Find gaps in understanding
- Suggest spikes or investigations

---

## OpenSpec Awareness

You have full context of the OpenSpec system. Use it naturally, don't force it.

### Check for context

At the start, quickly check what exists:
```bash
openspec list --json
```

This tells you:
- If there are active changes
- Their names, schemas, and status
- What the user might be working on

### When no change exists

Think freely. When insights crystallize, you might offer:

- "This feels solid enough to start a change. Want me to create one?"
  → Can transition to `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`
- Or keep exploring - no pressure to formalize

### When a change exists

If the user mentions a change or you detect one is relevant:

1. **Read existing artifacts for context**
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/proposal.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/design.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/tasks.md`
   - etc.

2. **Reference them naturally in conversation**
   - "Your design mentions using Redis, but we just realized SQLite fits better..."
   - "The proposal scopes this to premium users, but we're now thinking everyone..."

3. **Offer to capture when decisions are made**

   | Insight Type | Where to Capture |
   |--------------|------------------|
   | New requirement discovered | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Requirement changed | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Design decision made | `design.md` |
   | Scope changed | `proposal.md` |
   | New work identified | `tasks.md` |
   | Assumption invalidated | Relevant artifact |

   Example offers:
   - "That's a design decision. Capture it in design.md?"
   - "This is a new requirement. Add it to specs?"
   - "This changes scope. Update the proposal?"

4. **The user decides** - Offer and move on. Don't pressure. Don't auto-capture.

---

## What You Don't Have To Do

- Follow a script
- Ask the same questions every time
- Produce a specific artifact
- Reach a conclusion
- Stay on topic if a tangent is valuable
- Be brief (this is thinking time)

---

## Handling Different Entry Points

**User brings a vague idea:**
```
User: I'm thinking about adding real-time collaboration

You: Real-time collab is a big space. Let me think about this...

      COLLABORATION SPECTRUM
      ════════════════════════════════════════════

      Awareness          Coordination         Sync

          ▼                   ▼                 ▼

```

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐

     └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                        │
          ┌─────────────┼─────────────┐
          ▼             ▼             ▼

     │ Google  │  │  GitHub │  │  Email  │
     │  OAuth  │  │  OAuth  │  │  Magic  │
     └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘
          │             │             │
          └─────────────┼─────────────┘
                        ▼
                  ┌───────────┐
                  │  Session  │

                        │

```

     You're on task 4: "Implement OAuth flow"

     Let me trace what's involved...

     Or add a spike task to investigate?
```

**User wants to compare options:**
```
User: Should we use Postgres or SQLite?

You: Generic answer is boring. What's the context?

User: A CLI tool that tracks local dev environments

You: That changes everything.

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │         CLI TOOL DATA STORAGE                  │
     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     Key constraints:
     • No daemon running
     • Must work offline
     • Single user

                  SQLite          Postgres
     Deployment   embedded ✓      needs server ✗
     Offline      yes ✓           no ✗
     Single file  yes ✓           no ✗

     SQLite. Not even close.

     Unless... is there a sync component?
```

## Ending Discovery

There's no required ending. Discovery might:

- **Flow into action**: "Ready to start? /opsx:new or /opsx:ff"
- **Result in artifact updates**: "Updated design.md with these decisions"
- **Just provide clarity**: User has what they need, moves on
- **Continue later**: "We can pick this up anytime"

When it feels like things are crystallizing, you might summarize:

```
## What We Figured Out

**The problem**: [crystallized understanding]

**The approach**: [if one emerged]

**Open questions**: [if any remain]

**Next steps** (if ready):
- Create a change: /opsx:new <name>
- Fast-forward to tasks: /opsx:ff <name>
- Keep exploring: just keep talking
```

But this summary is optional. Sometimes the thinking IS the value.

---

## Guardrails

- **Don't implement** - Never write code or implement features. Creating OpenSpec artifacts is fine, writing application code is not.
- **Don't fake understanding** - If something is unclear, dig deeper
- **Don't rush** - Discovery is thinking time, not task time
- **Don't force structure** - Let patterns emerge naturally
- **Don't auto-capture** - Offer to save insights, don't just do it
- **Do visualize** - A good diagram is worth many paragraphs
- **Do explore the codebase** - Ground discussions in reality
- **Do question assumptions** - Including the user's and your own

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:37:33)

Perfect! The user wants to add patch storage to the design. Let me visualize how this would work.
## Agent (2026-04-09 02:37:33)

Great! So now you want to **archive each generated patch** in a folder. Let me think through this:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                  PATCH STORAGE ARCHITECTURE                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  Session Directory                                                  │
│       │                                                             │
│       ├── agent-workspace/   ← where agent works (fossil checkout)│
│       ├── upstream/            ← the git/fossil upstream repo       │
│       ├── repo.fossil         ← fossil history                      │
│       └── patches/            ← NEW: stored patches                │
│            ├── patch-001-2026-04-08T12-30-00.diff                  │
│            ├── patch-002-2026-04-08T14-15-30.diff                  │
│            └── patch-003-2026-04-08T16-45-00.diff                  │
│                                                                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Questions about patch storage:**

1. **Naming convention** - What do you want in the patch filename?
   - Sequential number (patch-001, patch-002...)
   - Timestamp (patch-2026-04-08T12-30-00)
   - Commit range (patch-abc123-to-def456.diff)
   - Session name + number (my-session-patch-001.diff)

2. **Metadata** - Store anything alongside the patch?
   ```
   patches/
   ├── patch-001.diff
   ├── patch-001.json   ← metadata (from/to commits, timestamp, stats)
   └── patch-002.diff
   ```

3. **Retention** - Keep all patches forever, or clean up old ones?

4. **Access** - How will patches be used?
   - User downloads them?
   - System replays them?
   - Both?

5. **Format** - Just the `.diff` file, or wrap it?

**And most importantly: What's the purpose?**
- **Audit trail** (see history of changes)?
- **Backup/restore** (can replay to recover)?
- **Code review** (human-readable patches)?
- **Debugging** (understand what went wrong)?

Also, should patches be **immutable** (never change once created) or **mutable** (can regenerate if needed)?

What's your thinking on these?

## User (2026-04-09 02:38:54)

nice let's called upstream-patch
1.commit range
2. good
3.forever
4.just keep as history for debugging purpoose
5. just plain diff

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:39:00)

The user has clarified the requirements for patch storage:

1. Folder name: `upstream-patch`
2. Naming: commit range (e.g., `patch-abc123-to-def456.diff`)
3. Metadata: yes (JSON alongside)
4. Retention: forever
5. Purpose: history for debugging
6. Format: plain diff

Now let me create a design document capturing this.
## Agent (2026-04-09 02:39:01)

Perfect! Let me capture this design:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    UPSTREAM-PATCH FOLDER DESIGN                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  Session Directory Structure                                        │
│  ==========================                                         │
│                                                                     │
│  session-12345/                                                     │
│       ├── agent-workspace/                                          │
│       ├── upstream/                                                   │
│       ├── repo.fossil                                                │
│       └── upstream-patch/               ← NEW FOLDER                │
│            ├── patch-abc123-to-def456.diff                          │
│            ├── patch-abc123-to-def456.json                          │
│            ├── patch-def456-to-ghi789.diff                          │
│            └── patch-def456-to-ghi789.json                          │
│                                                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  Naming Convention                                                  │
│  =================                                                  │
│                                                                     │
│  File:    patch-{FROM_COMMIT}-{SHORT}-to-{TO_COMMIT}-{SHORT}.diff  │
│  Example: patch-abc123-to-def456.diff                              │
│                                                                     │
│  JSON:    patch-{FROM_COMMIT}-to-{TO_COMMIT}.json                   │
│  Example: patch-abc123-to-def456.json                              │
│                                                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  JSON Metadata Structure                                            │
│  =========================                                          │
│                                                                     │
│  {                                                                   │
│    "generatedAt": "2026-04-08T12:30:00Z",                           │
│    "fromCommit": "abc123...",                                        │
│    "toCommit": "def456...",                                          │
│    "stats": {                                                        │
│      "filesAdded": 2,                                                │
│      "filesModified": 3,                                             │
│      "filesDeleted": 1,                                              │
│      "linesAdded": 45,                                               │
│      "linesDeleted": 12                                              │
│    },                                                                │
│    "sessionId": "session-12345"                                     │
│  }                                                                   │
│                                                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  Flow                                                               │
│  ====                                                               │
│                                                                     │
│  1. Work phase → commits in agent-workspace                         │
│  2. Click "Commit to Upstream"                                      │
│  3. System:                                                         │
│       a. Identify FROM (lastSyncedCommit) and TO (current HEAD)    │
│       b. Generate: fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v              │
│       c. Create patch file in upstream-patch/                       │
│       d. Create JSON metadata file                                  │
│       e. Apply patch to upstream/                                   │
│       f. Update lastSyncedCommit = TO                               │
│  4. Repeat...                                                        │
│                                                                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Open question:** Do you want to store the patch **before** applying it to upstream (so you have a record even if apply fails), or **only after successful apply**?

Also, should failed patch attempts be stored (with error info) or only successful ones?

**Ready to implement?** Want me to create the OpenSpec change with all the tasks?

i want the folder name upstream-patches

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│                                                                     │
│  Session Directory Structure                                        │
│  ==========================                                         │
│                                                                     │
│  session-12345/                                                     │
│       ├── agent-workspace/                                          │
│       ├── upstream/                                                   │
│       ├── repo.fossil                                                │
│       └── upstream-patches/             ← FOLDER NAME (plural)     │
│            ├── patch-abc123-to-def456.diff                          │
│            ├── patch-abc123-to-def456.json                          │
│            ├── patch-def456-to-ghi789.diff                          │

## OpenSpec Awareness

You have full context of the OpenSpec system. Use it naturally, don't force it.

### Check for context

At the start, quickly check what exists:
```bash
openspec list --json
```

This tells you:
- If there are active changes
- Their names, schemas, and status
- What the user might be working on

### When no change exists

Think freely. When insights crystallize, you might offer:

- "This feels solid enough to start a change. Want me to create one?"
  → Can transition to `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`
- Or keep exploring - no pressure to formalize

### When a change exists

If the user mentions a change or you detect one is relevant:

1. **Read existing artifacts for context**
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/proposal.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/design.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/tasks.md`
   - etc.

2. **Reference them naturally in conversation**
   - "Your design mentions using Redis, but we just realized SQLite fits better..."
   - "The proposal scopes this to premium users, but we're now thinking everyone..."

3. **Offer to capture when decisions are made**

   | Insight Type | Where to Capture |
   |--------------|------------------|
   | New requirement discovered | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Requirement changed | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |
   | Design decision made | `design.md` |
   | Scope changed | `proposal.md` |
   | New work identified | `tasks.md` |
   | Assumption invalidated | Relevant artifact |

   Example offers:
   - "That's a design decision. Capture it in design.md?"
   - "This is a new requirement. Add it to specs?"
   - "This changes scope. Update the proposal?"

4. **The user decides** - Offer and move on. Don't pressure. Don't auto-capture.

---

## What You Don't Have To Do

- Follow a script
- Ask the same questions every time
- Produce a specific artifact
- Reach a conclusion
- Stay on topic if a tangent is valuable
- Be brief (this is thinking time)

## Handling Different Entry Points

**User brings a vague idea:**
```
User: I'm thinking about adding real-time collaboration

You: Real-time collab is a big space. Let me think about this...

      COLLABORATION SPECTRUM
      ════════════════════════════════════════════

      Awareness          Coordination         Sync
          │                   │                 │
          ▼                   ▼                 ▼
      ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        ┌────────┐
      │Presence│         │Cursors │        │  CRDT  │
      │  "3    │         │ Multi  │        │Conflict│
      │online" │         │ select │        │  free  │
      └────────┘         └────────┘        └────────┘
          │                   │                 │
       trivial            moderate           complex

      Where's your head at?
```

**User brings a specific problem:**
```
User: The auth system is a mess

You: [reads codebase]

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │              CURRENT AUTH FLOW              │
     └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                        │
          ┌─────────────┼─────────────┐
          ▼             ▼             ▼
     ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌─────────┐
     │ Google  │  │  GitHub │  │  Email  │
     │  OAuth  │  │  OAuth  │  │  Magic  │
     └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘  └────┬────┘
          │             │             │
          └─────────────┼─────────────┘
                        ▼
                  ┌───────────┐
                  │  Session  │
                  └─────┬─────┘
                        │
                        ▼
                  ┌───────────┐
                  │   Perms   │
                  └───────────┘

     I see three tangles. Which one's burning?
```

**User is stuck mid-implementation:**
```
User: /opsx:explore add-auth-system
      The OAuth integration is more complex than expected

You: [reads change artifacts]

     You're on task 4: "Implement OAuth flow"

     Let me trace what's involved...

     [draws diagram, explores options, suggests paths]

     Want to update the design to reflect this?
     Or add a spike task to investigate?
```

**User wants to compare options:**
```
User: Should we use Postgres or SQLite?

You: Generic answer is boring. What's the context?

User: A CLI tool that tracks local dev environments

You: That changes everything.

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │         CLI TOOL DATA STORAGE                  │
     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     Key constraints:
     • No daemon running
     • Must work offline
     • Single user

                  SQLite          Postgres
     Deployment   embedded ✓      needs server ✗
     Offline      yes ✓           no ✗
     Single file  yes ✓           no ✗

     SQLite. Not even close.

     Unless... is there a sync component?
```

## Ending Discovery

There's no required ending. Discovery might:

- **Flow into action**: "Ready to start? /opsx:new or /opsx:ff"
- **Result in artifact updates**: "Updated design.md with these decisions"
- **Just provide clarity**: User has what they need, moves on
- **Continue later**: "We can pick this up anytime"

When it feels like things are crystallizing, you might summarize:

```
## What We Figured Out

**The problem**: [crystallized understanding]

**The approach**: [if one emerged]

**Open questions**: [if any remain]

**Next steps** (if ready):
- Create a change: /opsx:new <name>
- Fast-forward to tasks: /opsx:ff <name>
- Keep exploring: just keep talking
```

But this summary is optional. Sometimes the thinking IS the value.

---

## Guardrails

- **Don't implement** - Never write code or implement features. Creating OpenSpec artifacts is fine, writing application code is not.
- **Don't fake understanding** - If something is unclear, dig deeper
- **Don't rush** - Discovery is thinking time, not task time
- **Don't force structure** - Let patterns emerge naturally
- **Don't auto-capture** - Offer to save insights, don't just do it
- **Do visualize** - A good diagram is worth many paragraphs
- **Do explore the codebase** - Ground discussions in reality
- **Do question assumptions** - Including the user's and your own

## Agent (2026-04-09 02:40:39)

Perfect! Timestamp-based naming is more human-readable and naturally sorted.

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    UPSTREAM-PATCHES FOLDER                          │
│                    (Timestamp-Based Naming)                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  session-12345/                                                     │
│       ├── agent-workspace/                                          │
│       ├── upstream/                                                   │
│       ├── repo.fossil                                                │
│       └── upstream-patches/                                           │
│            ├── patch-2026-04-08-123045.diff                        │
│            ├── patch-2026-04-08-123045.json                        │
│            ├── patch-2026-04-08-141530.diff                        │
│            └── patch-2026-04-08-141530.json                        │
│                                                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  Naming Convention                                                  │
│  =================                                                  │
│                                                                     │
│  File:    patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.diff                             │
│  Example: patch-2026-04-08-123045.diff                               │
│                                                                     │
│  JSON:    patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.json                             │
│  Example: patch-2026-04-08-123045.json                               │
│                                                                     │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│  JSON Metadata (includes commit info)                               │
│  ======================================                             │
│                                                                     │
│  {                                                                   │
│    "generatedAt": "2026-04-08T12:30:45Z",                           │
│    "fromCommit": "abc123def456...",                                  │
│    "toCommit": "ghi789jkl012...",                                    │
│    "stats": {                                                        │
│      "filesAdded": 2,                                                │
│      "filesModified": 3,                                             │
│      "filesDeleted": 1                                               │
│    },                                                                │
│    "sessionId": "session-12345"                                     │
│  }                                                                   │
│                                                                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

The JSON still contains the commit range for debugging/traceability, but the filename is clean and timestamp-based.

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:42:01)

I have the instructions for the proposal artifact. Now I need to create it. Based on our exploration:

1. **Why**: Current file copying is fragile; patch-based sync is more reliable
2. **What Changes**: Replace manual copy with patch generation, store patches in upstream-patches/
3. **Capabilities**: New capability "patch-sync" for generating and applying patches
4. **Impact**: VCS module, commit service

Let me create the proposal file.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/proposal.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:42:10
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/proposal.md
content: ## Why

The current file synchronization from agent-workspace to upstream uses manual recursive copying, which is fragile and doesn't properly handle file deletions or renames. A patch-based approach using `fossil diff` will generate precise, reproducible diffs that work with both Git and Fossil upstreams, providing better reliability and an audit trail of changes.

## What Changes

- Replace `cleanCopyToUpstream()` method with patch-based sync
- Generate unified diff patches using `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
- Apply patches to upstream using `git apply` (Git) or `patch -p0` (Fossil)
- Store all generated patches in `upstream-patches/` folder with timestamp-based naming
- Track `lastSyncedCommit` in session to support incremental sync
- Store patch metadata (from/to commits, stats) alongside each patch file

## Capabilities

### New Capabilities
- `patch-sync`: Generate and apply unified diff patches from fossil commits to upstream repositories, with persistent storage of patch history for debugging

### Modified Capabilities
- None (this is an implementation detail change, not a requirements change)

## Impact

- **VCS Module** (`packages/mimo-platform/src/vcs/index.ts`): Replace `cleanCopyToUpstream()` with `generatePatch()` and `applyPatch()` methods
- **Commit Service** (`packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts`): Update commit flow to use patch-based sync
- **Session Repository**: Add `lastSyncedCommit` field to track sync state
- **Session Directory Structure**: New `upstream-patches/` folder for patch storage

│ changes │
╰─────────╯

@@ -0,0 +1,27 @@
+## Why
+
+The current file synchronization from agent-workspace to upstream uses manual recursive copying, which is fragile and doesn't properly handle file deletions or renames. A patch-based approach using `fossil diff` will generate precise, reproducible diffs that work with both Git and Fossil upstreams, providing better reliability and an audit trail of changes.
+
+## What Changes
+
+- Replace `cleanCopyToUpstream()` method with patch-based sync
+- Generate unified diff patches using `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
+- Apply patches to upstream using `git apply` (Git) or `patch -p0` (Fossil)
+- Store all generated patches in `upstream-patches/` folder with timestamp-based naming
+- Track `lastSyncedCommit` in session to support incremental sync
+- Store patch metadata (from/to commits, stats) alongside each patch file
+
+## Capabilities
+
+### New Capabilities
+- `patch-sync`: Generate and apply unified diff patches from fossil commits to upstream repositories, with persistent storage of patch history for debugging
+
+### Modified Capabilities
+- None (this is an implementation detail change, not a requirements change)
+
+## Impact
+
+- **VCS Module** (`packages/mimo-platform/src/vcs/index.ts`): Replace `cleanCopyToUpstream()` with `generatePatch()` and `applyPatch()` methods
+- **Commit Service** (`packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts`): Update commit flow to use patch-based sync
+- **Session Repository**: Add `lastSyncedCommit` field to track sync state
+- **Session Directory Structure**: New `upstream-patches/` folder for patch storage

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-09 02:44:09)

I have both design and specs ready to create. Let me create both artifacts. Since they don't depend on each other (both only depend on proposal which is done), I can create them in parallel.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/design.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:44:25
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/design.md
content: ## Context

Currently, the system copies files from agent-workspace to upstream using `cleanCopyToUpstream()` which performs a manual recursive file copy. This approach:
- Doesn't properly track what changed (hard to debug)
- Uses file-by-file comparison which is fragile
- Doesn't preserve the semantic meaning of changes (adds vs modifies vs deletes)
- Has no audit trail of what was synced

The new patch-based approach uses Fossil's native diff capability to generate unified diffs that capture exact changes between commits, which can be applied to both Git and Fossil upstreams.

## Goals / Non-Goals

**Goals:**
- Replace manual file copying with patch-based synchronization
- Generate patches using `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
- Support both Git and Fossil upstream repositories
- Store all patches in `upstream-patches/` folder with timestamp-based naming
- Track `lastSyncedCommit` for incremental sync
- Store patch metadata (commits, stats) alongside each patch

**Non-Goals:**
- Full bidirectional sync (only agent-workspace → upstream)
- Real-time synchronization
- Conflict resolution (assume upstream doesn't change between syncs)
- Binary file diff optimization

## Decisions

### Patch Format: Unified Diff
**Decision:** Use `fossil diff -v` (verbose unified diff)
**Rationale:** Unified diff is the de facto standard. Tested and confirmed to work with both `git apply` and `patch -p0`.
**Alternative considered:** Fossil's binary patch format (`fossil patch`) - rejected because it's Fossil-specific and wouldn't work with Git upstreams.

### Naming: Timestamps vs Commit Hashes
**Decision:** Use timestamp-based filenames (`patch-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.diff`)
**Rationale:** Human-readable, naturally sorted, easy to identify when patch was created
**Alternative considered:** Commit hashes (`patch-abc123-to-def456.diff`) - rejected because timestamps are more user-friendly for debugging

### Storage Location: Session-scoped
**Decision:** Store patches in `upstream-patches/` folder within each session directory
**Rationale:** Patches belong to the session they were generated from. Isolated per session prevents cross-contamination.
**Alternative considered:** Global patch storage - rejected because patches are session-specific

### Sync Strategy: Incremental with State Tracking
**Decision:** Track `lastSyncedCommit` in session database
**Rationale:** Enables incremental sync (only sync new commits since last sync)
**Alternative considered:** Full diff every time - rejected because it's inefficient and creates duplicate patches

### Apply Strategy: Direct Apply
**Decision:** Apply patches directly to upstream working tree
**Rationale:** Simplest approach. Git and Fossil both support applying unified diffs.
**Alternative considered:** Import as commits - rejected because it complicates the flow and may conflict with upstream's existing history

## Risks / Trade-offs

- **[Risk]** Patch application may fail if upstream files changed between syncs → **Mitigation:** Detect dirty state before applying, provide clear error message
- **[Risk]** Binary files not handled well by unified diff → **Mitigation:** Document limitation, copy binary files separately if needed
- **[Risk]** File permissions not preserved in unified diff → **Mitigation:** Acceptable trade-off for text files; document limitation
- **[Risk]** Conflicts if user modifies upstream manually → **Mitigation:** Check for uncommitted changes before applying patch

## Migration Plan

1. **Phase 1:** Implement new methods in VCS module (`generatePatch`, `applyPatch`)
2. **Phase 2:** Update commit service to use new methods
3. **Phase 3:** Add `lastSyncedCommit` tracking to session repository
4. **Phase 4:** Test with both Git and Fossil upstreams
5. **Phase 5:** Remove legacy `cleanCopyToUpstream` method

## Open Questions

- Should we validate patch before storing it (dry-run apply)?
- Should failed patch applications be stored for debugging?


```
Wrote file successfully.





╭─────────╮
│ changes │
╰─────────╯

@@ -0,0 +1,72 @@
+## Context
+
+Currently, the system copies files from agent-workspace to upstream using `cleanCopyToUpstream()` which performs a manual recursive file copy. This approach:
+- Doesn't properly track what changed (hard to debug)
+- Uses file-by-file comparison which is fragile
+- Doesn't preserve the semantic meaning of changes (adds vs modifies vs deletes)
+- Has no audit trail of what was synced
+
+The new patch-based approach uses Fossil's native diff capability to generate unified diffs that capture exact changes between commits, which can be applied to both Git and Fossil upstreams.
+
+## Goals / Non-Goals
+
+**Goals:**
+- Replace manual file copying with patch-based synchronization
+- Generate patches using `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
+- Support both Git and Fossil upstream repositories
+- Store all patches in `upstream-patches/` folder with timestamp-based naming
+- Track `lastSyncedCommit` for incremental sync
+- Store patch metadata (commits, stats) alongside each patch
+
+**Non-Goals:**
+- Full bidirectional sync (only agent-workspace → upstream)
+- Real-time synchronization
+- Conflict resolution (assume upstream doesn't change between syncs)
+- Binary file diff optimization
+
+## Decisions
+
+### Patch Format: Unified Diff
+**Decision:** Use `fossil diff -v` (verbose unified diff)
+**Rationale:** Unified diff is the de facto standard. Tested and confirmed to work with both `git apply` and `patch -p0`.
+**Alternative considered:** Fossil's binary patch format (`fossil patch`) - rejected because it's Fossil-specific and wouldn't work with Git upstreams.
+
+### Naming: Timestamps vs Commit Hashes
+**Decision:** Use timestamp-based filenames (`patch-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.diff`)
+**Rationale:** Human-readable, naturally sorted, easy to identify when patch was created
+**Alternative considered:** Commit hashes (`patch-abc123-to-def456.diff`) - rejected because timestamps are more user-friendly for debugging
+
+### Storage Location: Session-scoped
+**Decision:** Store patches in `upstream-patches/` folder within each session directory
+**Rationale:** Patches belong to the session they were generated from. Isolated per session prevents cross-contamination.
+**Alternative considered:** Global patch storage - rejected because patches are session-specific
+
+### Sync Strategy: Incremental with State Tracking
+**Decision:** Track `lastSyncedCommit` in session database
+**Rationale:** Enables incremental sync (only sync new commits since last sync)
+**Alternative considered:** Full diff every time - rejected because it's inefficient and creates duplicate patches
+
+### Apply Strategy: Direct Apply
+**Decision:** Apply patches directly to upstream working tree
+**Rationale:** Simplest approach. Git and Fossil both support applying unified diffs.
+**Alternative considered:** Import as commits - rejected because it complicates the flow and may conflict with upstream's existing history
+
+## Risks / Trade-offs
+
+- **[Risk]** Patch application may fail if upstream files changed between syncs → **Mitigation:** Detect dirty state before applying, provide clear error message
+- **[Risk]** Binary files not handled well by unified diff → **Mitigation:** Document limitation, copy binary files separately if needed
+- **[Risk]** File permissions not preserved in unified diff → **Mitigation:** Acceptable trade-off for text files; document limitation
+- **[Risk]** Conflicts if user modifies upstream manually → **Mitigation:** Check for uncommitted changes before applying patch
+
+## Migration Plan
+
+1. **Phase 1:** Implement new methods in VCS module (`generatePatch`, `applyPatch`)
+2. **Phase 2:** Update commit service to use new methods
+3. **Phase 3:** Add `lastSyncedCommit` tracking to session repository
+4. **Phase 4:** Test with both Git and Fossil upstreams
+5. **Phase 5:** Remove legacy `cleanCopyToUpstream` method
+
+## Open Questions
+
+- Should we validate patch before storing it (dry-run apply)?
+- Should failed patch applications be stored for debugging?
```


### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/specs/patch-sync/spec.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:44:25
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/specs/patch-sync/spec.md
content: ## ADDED Requirements

### Requirement: Generate unified diff patch
The system SHALL generate a unified diff patch representing changes between two fossil commits.

#### Scenario: Generate patch from session commits
- **WHEN** the system generates a patch from the session's `lastSyncedCommit` to the current HEAD
- **THEN** it SHALL execute `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
- **AND** the output SHALL be a valid unified diff format

### Requirement: Store patch in upstream-patches folder
The system SHALL store each generated patch in a session-scoped `upstream-patches/` folder.

#### Scenario: Create patch file with timestamp name
- **WHEN** a patch is generated
- **THEN** it SHALL be saved as `upstream-patches/patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.diff`
- **AND** a corresponding JSON metadata file SHALL be created as `upstream-patches/patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.json`

#### Scenario: Store patch metadata
- **WHEN** a patch is stored
- **THEN** the JSON file SHALL include:
  - `generatedAt`: ISO 8601 timestamp
  - `fromCommit`: Hash of starting commit
  - `toCommit`: Hash of ending commit
  - `stats`: Object with file counts (added, modified, deleted)

### Requirement: Apply patch to Git upstream
The system SHALL apply generated patches to Git upstream repositories.

#### Scenario: Apply unified diff to Git
- **WHEN** applying a patch to a Git upstream
- **THEN** the system SHALL execute `git apply patch.diff`
- **AND** file modifications SHALL be staged in the working tree
- **AND** new files SHALL appear as untracked

### Requirement: Apply patch to Fossil upstream
The system SHALL apply generated patches to Fossil upstream repositories.

#### Scenario: Apply unified diff to Fossil
- **WHEN** applying a patch to a Fossil upstream
- **THEN** the system SHALL execute `patch -p0 < patch.diff`
- **AND** all changes SHALL be applied to the working tree

### Requirement: Track last synced commit
The system SHALL track the last successfully synced commit for each session.

#### Scenario: Update sync state after successful patch
- **WHEN** a patch is successfully applied to upstream
- **THEN** the session's `lastSyncedCommit` SHALL be updated to the `toCommit` value
- **AND** this value SHALL be used as the `fromCommit` for the next patch generation

### Requirement: Create upstream-patches folder on demand
The system SHALL create the `upstream-patches/` folder when first needed.

#### Scenario: First patch generation
- **WHEN** generating the first patch for a session
- **THEN** the system SHALL create `upstream-patches/` directory if it doesn't exist

content: ## 1. VCS Module - Patch Generation

- [ ] 2.1 Add `applyPatchToGit()` method that executes `git apply patch.diff`
- [ ] 2.2 Add `applyPatchToFossil()` method that executes `patch -p0 < patch.diff`
- [ ] 2.3 Add `checkUpstreamStatus()` method to verify upstream is clean before applying
- [ ] 2.4 Implement patch application with proper error handling

## 3. Patch Storage

- [ ] 3.1 Create `ensureUpstreamPatchesDir()` helper to create `upstream-patches/` folder
- [ ] 3.2 Implement `generatePatchFilename()` using timestamp format `patch-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.diff`
- [ ] 3.3 Implement `writePatchFile()` to save diff content to file

- [ ] 4.4 Add `sessionRepository.updateLastSyncedCommit(sessionId, commitHash)` method

- [ ] 5.3 Add logic to get `toCommit` (current HEAD)

- [ ] 5.5 Call appropriate `applyPatch()` method based on `repoType`
- [ ] 5.6 Update `lastSyncedCommit` after successful patch application
- [ ] 5.7 Update commit message generation to include patch reference

- [ ] 6.1 Test patch generation creates valid unified diff
- [ ] 6.2 Test patch applies successfully to Git upstream
- [ ] 6.3 Test patch applies successfully to Fossil upstream
- [ ] 6.4 Test `upstream-patches/` folder is created on first patch
- [ ] 6.5 Test JSON metadata file is created with correct fields
- [ ] 6.6 Test incremental sync (only syncs new commits since last sync)
- [ ] 6.7 Test error handling when upstream has uncommitted changes
- [ ] 6.8 Test error handling when patch application fails

- [ ] 7.2 Remove any helper methods only used by `cleanCopyToUpstream()`
- [ ] 7.3 Update any tests that relied on `cleanCopyToUpstream()`

- [ ] 8.2 Document the `upstream-patches/` folder structure
- [ ] 8.3 Add troubleshooting guide for patch application failures
- [ ] 8.4 Document known limitations (binary files, permissions)

+## 3. Patch Storage
+
+- [ ] 3.1 Create `ensureUpstreamPatchesDir()` helper to create `upstream-patches/` folder
+- [ ] 3.2 Implement `generatePatchFilename()` using timestamp format `patch-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.diff`
+- [ ] 3.3 Implement `writePatchFile()` to save diff content to file
+- [ ] 3.4 Implement `writePatchMetadata()` to save JSON with fromCommit, toCommit, stats
+- [ ] 3.5 Parse diff output to count added/modified/deleted files for metadata stats
+
+## 4. Session Repository Updates
+
+- [ ] 4.1 Add `lastSyncedCommit` column to sessions table in database schema
+- [ ] 4.2 Update `Session` type/interface to include `lastSyncedCommit?: string`
+- [ ] 4.3 Update `sessionRepository.findById()` to include `lastSyncedCommit` field
+- [ ] 4.4 Add `sessionRepository.updateLastSyncedCommit(sessionId, commitHash)` method
+
+## 5. Commit Service Integration
+
+- [ ] 5.1 Update `commitAndPush()` to call `vcs.generatePatch()` instead of `cleanCopyToUpstream()`
+- [ ] 5.2 Add logic to determine `fromCommit` (use `lastSyncedCommit` or get first commit)
+- [ ] 5.3 Add logic to get `toCommit` (current HEAD)
+- [ ] 5.4 Store patch in `upstream-patches/` folder before applying
+- [ ] 5.5 Call appropriate `applyPatch()` method based on `repoType`
+- [ ] 5.6 Update `lastSyncedCommit` after successful patch application
+- [ ] 5.7 Update commit message generation to include patch reference
+
+## 6. Testing
+
+- [ ] 6.1 Test patch generation creates valid unified diff
+- [ ] 6.2 Test patch applies successfully to Git upstream
+- [ ] 6.3 Test patch applies successfully to Fossil upstream
+- [ ] 6.4 Test `upstream-patches/` folder is created on first patch
+- [ ] 6.5 Test JSON metadata file is created with correct fields
+- [ ] 6.6 Test incremental sync (only syncs new commits since last sync)
+- [ ] 6.7 Test error handling when upstream has uncommitted changes
+- [ ] 6.8 Test error handling when patch application fails
+
+## 7. Cleanup
+
+- [ ] 7.1 Remove legacy `cleanCopyToUpstream()` method from VCS class
+- [ ] 7.2 Remove any helper methods only used by `cleanCopyToUpstream()`
+- [ ] 7.3 Update any tests that relied on `cleanCopyToUpstream()`
+- [ ] 7.4 Verify no references to old method remain in codebase
+
+## 8. Documentation
+
+- [ ] 8.1 Update VCS module documentation to describe patch-based approach
+- [ ] 8.2 Document the `upstream-patches/` folder structure
+- [ ] 8.3 Add troubleshooting guide for patch application failures
+- [ ] 8.4 Document known limitations (binary files, permissions)
```

<skill_content name="openspec-apply-change">
# Skill: openspec-apply-change

Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.

**Input**: Optionally specify a change name. If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.

**Steps**

1. **Select the change**

   If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
   - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
   - Auto-select if only one active change exists
   - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select

   Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).

2. **Check status to understand the schema**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to understand:
   - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
   - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)

3. **Get apply instructions**

   ```bash
   openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
   ```

   This returns:
   - Context file paths (varies by schema - could be proposal/specs/design/tasks or spec/tests/implementation/docs)
   - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
   - Task list with status
   - Dynamic instruction based on current state

   **Handle states:**
   - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using openspec-continue-change
   - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
   - Otherwise: proceed to implementation

4. **Read context files**

   Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
   The files depend on the schema being used:
   - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
   - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output

5. **Show current progress**

   Display:
   - Schema being used
   - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
   - Remaining tasks overview
   - Dynamic instruction from CLI

6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**

   For each pending task:
   - Show which task is being worked on
   - Make the code changes required
   - Keep changes minimal and focused
   - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
   - Continue to next task

   **Pause if:**
   - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
   - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
   - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
   - User interrupts

7. **On completion or pause, show status**

   Display:
   - Tasks completed this session
   - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
   - If all done: suggest archive
   - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance

**Output During Implementation**

```

✓ Task complete

[...implementation happening...]
✓ Task complete
```

- [x] Task 1
- [x] Task 2
...

All tasks complete! Ready to archive this change.
```

<description of the issue>

2. <option 2>
3. Other approach

What would you like to do?
```

- Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
- If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
- If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
- Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
- Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
- Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
- Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/specs/patch-sync/spec.md

**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:46:51
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/specs/patch-sync/spec.md

```
<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/specs/patch-sync/spec.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: ## ADDED Requirements
2: 
3: ### Requirement: Generate unified diff patch
4: The system SHALL generate a unified diff patch representing changes between two fossil commits.
5: 
6: #### Scenario: Generate patch from session commits
7: - **WHEN** the system generates a patch from the session's `lastSyncedCommit` to the current HEAD
8: - **THEN** it SHALL execute `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
9: - **AND** the output SHALL be a valid unified diff format
10: 
11: ### Requirement: Store patch in upstream-patches folder
12: The system SHALL store each generated patch in a session-scoped `upstream-patches/` folder.
13: 
14: #### Scenario: Create patch file with timestamp name
15: - **WHEN** a patch is generated
16: - **THEN** it SHALL be saved as `upstream-patches/patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.diff`
17: - **AND** a corresponding JSON metadata file SHALL be created as `upstream-patches/patch-{YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS}.json`
18: 
19: #### Scenario: Store patch metadata
20: - **WHEN** a patch is stored
21: - **THEN** the JSON file SHALL include:
22:   - `generatedAt`: ISO 8601 timestamp
23:   - `fromCommit`: Hash of starting commit
24:   - `toCommit`: Hash of ending commit
25:   - `stats`: Object with file counts (added, modified, deleted)
26: 
27: ### Requirement: Apply patch to Git upstream
28: The system SHALL apply generated patches to Git upstream repositories.
29: 
30: #### Scenario: Apply unified diff to Git
31: - **WHEN** applying a patch to a Git upstream
32: - **THEN** the system SHALL execute `git apply patch.diff`
33: - **AND** file modifications SHALL be staged in the working tree
34: - **AND** new files SHALL appear as untracked
35: 
36: ### Requirement: Apply patch to Fossil upstream
37: The system SHALL apply generated patches to Fossil upstream repositories.
38: 
39: #### Scenario: Apply unified diff to Fossil
40: - **WHEN** applying a patch to a Fossil upstream
41: - **THEN** the system SHALL execute `patch -p0 < patch.diff`
42: - **AND** all changes SHALL be applied to the working tree
43: 
44: ### Requirement: Track last synced commit
45: The system SHALL track the last successfully synced commit for each session.
46: 
47: #### Scenario: Update sync state after successful patch
48: - **WHEN** a patch is successfully applied to upstream
49: - **THEN** the session's `lastSyncedCommit` SHALL be updated to the `toCommit` value
50: - **AND** this value SHALL be used as the `fromCommit` for the next patch generation
51: 
52: ### Requirement: Create upstream-patches folder on demand
53: The system SHALL create the `upstream-patches/` folder when first needed.
54: 
55: #### Scenario: First patch generation
56: - **WHEN** generating the first patch for a session
57: - **THEN** the system SHALL create `upstream-patches/` directory if it doesn't exist

(End of file - total 57 lines)
</content>
```


### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/design.md

**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:46:51
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/design.md

```
<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/patch-based-sync/design.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: ## Context
2: 
3: Currently, the system copies files from agent-workspace to upstream using `cleanCopyToUpstream()` which performs a manual recursive file copy. This approach:
4: - Doesn't properly track what changed (hard to debug)
5: - Uses file-by-file comparison which is fragile
6: - Doesn't preserve the semantic meaning of changes (adds vs modifies vs deletes)
7: - Has no audit trail of what was synced
8: 
9: The new patch-based approach uses Fossil's native diff capability to generate unified diffs that capture exact changes between commits, which can be applied to both Git and Fossil upstreams.
10: 
11: ## Goals / Non-Goals
12: 
13: **Goals:**
14: - Replace manual file copying with patch-based synchronization
15: - Generate patches using `fossil diff --from $FROM --to $TO -v`
16: - Support both Git and Fossil upstream repositories
17: - Store all patches in `upstream-patches/` folder with timestamp-based naming
18: - Track `lastSyncedCommit` for incremental sync
19: - Store patch metadata (commits, stats) alongside each patch
20: 
21: **Non-Goals:**
22: - Full bidirectional sync (only agent-workspace → upstream)
23: - Real-time synchronization
24: - Conflict resolution (assume upstream doesn't change between syncs)
25: - Binary file diff optimization
26: 
27: ## Decisions
28: 
29: ### Patch Format: Unified Diff
30: **Decision:** Use `fossil diff -v` (verbose unified diff)
31: **Rationale:** Unified diff is the de facto standard. Tested and confirmed to work with both `git apply` and `patch -p0`.
32: **Alternative considered:** Fossil's binary patch format (`fossil patch`) - rejected because it's Fossil-specific and wouldn't work with Git upstreams.
33: 
34: ### Naming: Timestamps vs Commit Hashes
35: **Decision:** Use timestamp-based filenames (`patch-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.diff`)
36: **Rationale:** Human-readable, naturally sorted, easy to identify when patch was created
37: **Alternative considered:** Commit hashes (`patch-abc123-to-def456.diff`) - rejected because timestamps are more user-friendly for debugging
38: 
39: ### Storage Location: Session-scoped
40: **Decision:** Store patches in `upstream-patches/` folder within each session directory
41: **Rationale:** Patches belong to the session they were generated from. Isolated per session prevents cross-contamination.
42: **Alternative considered:** Global patch storage - rejected because patches are session-specific
43: 
44: ### Sync Strategy: Incremental with State Tracking
45: **Decision:** Track `lastSyncedCommit` in session database
46: **Rationale:** Enables incremental sync (only sync new commits since last sync)
47: **Alternative considered:** Full diff every time - rejected because it's inefficient and creates duplicate patches
48: 
49: ### Apply Strategy: Direct Apply
50: **Decision:** Apply patches directly to upstream working tree
51: **Rationale:** Simplest approach. Git and Fossil both support applying unified diffs.
52: **Alternative considered:** Import as commits - rejected because it complicates the flow and may conflict with upstream's existing history
53: 
54: ## Risks / Trade-offs
55: 
56: - **[Risk]** Patch application may fail if upstream files changed between syncs → **Mitigation:** Detect dirty state before applying, provide clear error message
57: - **[Risk]** Binary files not handled well by unified diff → **Mitigation:** Document limitation, copy binary files separately if needed
58: - **[Risk]** File permissions not preserved in unified diff → **Mitigation:** Acceptable trade-off for text files; document limitation
59: - **[Risk]** Conflicts if user modifies upstream manually → **Mitigation:** Check for uncommitted changes before applying patch
60: 
61: ## Migration Plan
62: 
63: 1. **Phase 1:** Implement new methods in VCS module (`generatePatch`, `applyPatch`)
64: 2. **Phase 2:** Update commit service to use new methods
65: 3. **Phase 3:** Add `lastSyncedCommit` tracking to session repository
66: 4. **Phase 4:** Test with both Git and Fossil upstreams
67: 5. **Phase 5:** Remove legacy `cleanCopyToUpstream` method
68: 
69: ## Open Questions
70: 
71: - Should we validate patch before storing it (dry-run apply)?
72: - Should failed patch applications be stored for debugging?

(End of file - total 72 lines)
</content>
```

13: export class VCS {
14:   private async execCommand(
15:     command: string[],
16:     cwd?: string,
17:     env?: Record<string, string>
18:   ): Promise<{ success: boolean; output: string; error: string }> {
19:     const proc = Bun.spawn(command, {
20:       cwd,
21:       stdout: "pipe",
22:       stderr: "pipe",
23:       env: env ? { ...process.env, ...env } : undefined,
24:     });
25: 
26:     const exitCode = await proc.exited;
27:     const stdout = await new Response(proc.stdout).text();
28:     const stderr = await new Response(proc.stderr).text();
29: 
30:     return {
31:       success: exitCode === 0,
32:       output: stdout.trim(),
33:       error: stderr.trim(),
34:     };
35:   }
36: 
37:   // Helper to inject HTTPS credentials into URL
38:   private injectHttpsCredentials(repoUrl: string, credential: Extract<Credential, { type: "https" }>): string {
39:     try {
40:       const url = new URL(repoUrl);
41:       url.username = encodeURIComponent(credential.username);
42:       url.password = encodeURIComponent(credential.password);
43:       return url.toString();
44:     } catch {
45:       // If URL parsing fails, assume it's SSH format and return as-is
46:       return repoUrl;
47:     }
48:   }
49: 
50:   // Helper to create temporary SSH key file
51:   private createTempSshKeyFile(privateKey: string): string {

54:     writeFileSync(keyFile, privateKey, { mode: 0o600 });
55:     chmodSync(keyFile, 0o600);
56:     return keyFile;
57:   }
58: 
59:   // Helper to delete temporary SSH key file
60:   private deleteTempSshKeyFile(keyPath: string): void {
61:     try {
62:       unlinkSync(keyPath);
63:     } catch {
64:       // Ignore errors during cleanup
65:     }
66:   }
67: 
68:   // Helper to build SSH command for GIT_SSH_COMMAND
69:   private buildGitSshCommand(keyPath: string): string {
70:     return `ssh -i "${keyPath}" -o IdentitiesOnly=yes -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null`;
71:   }

73:   // Helper to detect if URL is SSH

76:   }

78:   // Helper to check if error is authentication-related
79:   private isAuthError(error: string, type: "https" | "ssh"): boolean {
80:     const lowerError = error.toLowerCase();
81:     
82:     // Exclude network errors first
83:     if (lowerError.includes("timeout") || 
84:         lowerError.includes("could not resolve") ||
85:         lowerError.includes("network is unreachable") ||
86:         lowerError.includes("no route to host")) {
87:       return false;
88:     }
89:     
90:     if (type === "https") {
91:       return lowerError.includes("authentication failed") ||
92:              lowerError.includes("403") ||
93:              lowerError.includes("401") ||
94:              lowerError.includes("unauthorized");
95:     } else {
96:       return lowerError.includes("permission denied") ||
97:              lowerError.includes("publickey") ||
98:              lowerError.includes("authentication") ||
99:              lowerError.includes("host key verification failed");
100:     }

757:   async fossilUp(agentWorkspacePath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
758:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "up"], agentWorkspacePath);
759:     return {
760:       success: result.success,
761:       output: result.output,
762:       error: result.error || undefined,
763:     };
764:   }
765: 
766:   async cleanCopyToUpstream(
767:     agentWorkspacePath: string,
768:     upstreamPath: string
769:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
770:     const { readdirSync, statSync, copyFileSync, mkdirSync, unlinkSync, rmdirSync } = await import("fs");
771:     const { join, relative } = await import("path");
772: 
773:     const { existsSync: fsExistsSync } = await import("fs");
774:     
775:     try {
776:       // Step 1: Get list of files that SHOULD exist according to fossil
777:       // These are the files tracked in the current checkout
778:       const fossilTrackedFiles: Set<string> = new Set();
779:       const fossilLsResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "ls"], agentWorkspacePath);
780:       if (fossilLsResult.success && fossilLsResult.output) {
781:         const lines = fossilLsResult.output.split("\n").filter(line => line.trim());
782:         for (const line of lines) {
783:           fossilTrackedFiles.add(line.trim());
784:         }
785:       }
786: 
787:       // Step 2: Get list of tracked files in upstream (source of truth for deletions)
788:       const upstreamTrackedFiles: string[] = [];
789:       if (fsExistsSync(upstreamPath)) {
790:         const gitLsResult = await this.execCommand(["git", "ls-files"], upstreamPath);
791:         if (gitLsResult.success && gitLsResult.output) {
792:           const lines = gitLsResult.output.split("\n").filter(line => line.trim());
793:           upstreamTrackedFiles.push(...lines);
794:         }
795:       }
796: 
797:       // Step 3: Copy all files from agent-workspace to upstream
798:       // Exclude VCS metadata directories
799:       // Files on disk but NOT in fossil ls are either:
800:       // - Untracked files (should be copied)
801:       // - Deleted tracked files (should NOT be copied)
802:       const excludeItems = new Set([".git", ".fossil", ".fslckout"]);
803:       
804:       const copyRecursive = (source: string, dest: string, basePath: string = source) => {
805:         if (!fsExistsSync(source)) return;
806: 
807:         const entries = readdirSync(source, { withFileTypes: true });
808:         for (const entry of entries) {
809:           // Skip VCS metadata directories
810:           if (excludeItems.has(entry.name)) continue;
811: 
812:           const sourcePath = join(source, entry.name);
813:           const destPath = join(dest, entry.name);
814:           const relativePath = relative(basePath, sourcePath);
815: 
816:           if (entry.isDirectory()) {
817:             if (!fsExistsSync(destPath)) {
818:               mkdirSync(destPath, { recursive: true });
819:             }
820:             copyRecursive(sourcePath, destPath, basePath);
821:           } else {
822:             // Only copy if file should exist according to fossil,
823:             // OR if it's not tracked at all (new untracked file)
824:             const shouldCopy = fossilTrackedFiles.has(relativePath) || !upstreamTrackedFiles.includes(relativePath);
825:             if (shouldCopy) {
826:               copyFileSync(sourcePath, destPath);
827:             }
828:           }
829:         }
830:       };
831: 
832:       if (fsExistsSync(agentWorkspacePath)) {
833:         copyRecursive(agentWorkspacePath, upstreamPath, agentWorkspacePath);
834:       }
835: 
836:       // Step 4: Delete from upstream files that are:
837:       // - Tracked in upstream (from git ls-files)
838:       // - Either not on agent disk OR not tracked by fossil (meaning deleted)
839:       for (const trackedFile of upstreamTrackedFiles) {
840:         const agentFilePath = join(agentWorkspacePath, trackedFile);
841:         const upstreamFilePath = join(upstreamPath, trackedFile);
842:         
843:         // Delete if tracked in upstream but either:
844:         // 1. Not present on agent disk, OR
845:         // 2. Present on disk but NOT tracked by fossil (was deleted via fossil rm)
846:         const existsOnDisk = fsExistsSync(agentFilePath);
847:         const trackedByFossil = fossilTrackedFiles.has(trackedFile);
848:         const shouldDelete = !existsOnDisk || !trackedByFossil;
849:         
850:         if (shouldDelete && fsExistsSync(upstreamFilePath)) {
851:           unlinkSync(upstreamFilePath);
852:           
853:           // Clean up empty parent directories
854:           let parentDir = join(upstreamPath, trackedFile);
855:           while (true) {
856:             parentDir = join(parentDir, "..");
857:             const resolvedParent = join(parentDir); // Normalize
858:             if (resolvedParent === upstreamPath) break;
859:             
860:             try {
861:               const entries = readdirSync(resolvedParent);
862:               if (entries.length === 0) {
863:                 rmdirSync(resolvedParent);
864:               } else {
865:                 break;
866:               }
867:             } catch {
868:               break;
869:             }
870:           }
871:         }
872:       }
873: 
874:       return {
875:         success: true,
876:         output: "Files copied successfully",
877:       };
878:     } catch (error) {
879:       return {
880:         success: false,
881:         error: `Failed to copy files: ${error}`,
882:       };
883:     }
884:   }
885: 
886:   async commitUpstream(
887:     upstreamPath: string,
888:     repoType: "git" | "fossil"
889:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
890:     const message = `Mimo commit at ${new Date().toISOString()}`;
891: 
892:     if (repoType === "git") {
893:       // Git: add all and commit
894:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["git", "add", "-A"], upstreamPath);
895:       if (!addResult.success) {
896:         return {
897:           success: false,
898:           output: addResult.output,
899:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
900:         };
901:       }
902: 
903:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
904:         ["git", "commit", "-m", message],
905:         upstreamPath
906:       );
907: 
908:       // Check if nothing to commit
909:       if (commitResult.error?.includes("nothing to commit") || 
910:           commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit")) {
911:         return {
912:           success: true,
913:           output: "No changes to commit",
914:         };
915:       }
916: 
917:       return {
918:         success: commitResult.success,
919:         output: commitResult.output,
920:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
921:       };
922:     } else {
923:       // Fossil: addremove and commit
924:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "addremove"], upstreamPath);
925:       if (!addResult.success) {
926:         return {
927:           success: false,
928:           output: addResult.output,
929:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
930:         };
931:       }
932: 
933:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
934:         ["fossil", "commit", "-m", message],
935:         upstreamPath
936:       );
937: 
938:       return {
939:         success: commitResult.success,
940:         output: commitResult.output,
941:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
942:       };
943:     }
944:   }
945:

948:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
949:     credential?: Credential,

77:     const sessionPath = this.getSessionPath(input.projectId, id);

79:     const agentWorkspacePath = this.getAgentWorkspacePath(input.projectId, id);
80:

89:     }

94:     }

111:     };
112:

115:       dump(sessionData),

145:               ...data,
146:               agentWorkspacePath: data.agentWorkspacePath || (data as any).checkoutPath,
147:             };
148:             return {
149:               ...sessionData,
150:               createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
151:               updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
152:             };

156:     }
157:

159:   }

171:       ...data,

190:

194:         if (existsSync(sessionFile)) {

196:           const data = load(content) as SessionData;

201:           };
202:           sessions.push({
203:             ...sessionData,
204:             createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
205:             updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
206:           });
207:         }
208:       }
209:     }
210: 
211:     return sessions.sort((a, b) => b.createdAt.getTime() - a.createdAt.getTime());
212:   }

214:   async findByAssignedAgentId(agentId: string): Promise<Session[]> {

219: 
220:     const projectEntries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
221:     const sessions: Session[] = [];
222:

225:         const sessionsDir = join(Paths.projects, projectEntry.name, "sessions");
226:         if (existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
227:           const entries = readdirSync(sessionsDir, { withFileTypes: true });
228:           for (const entry of entries) {
229:             if (entry.isDirectory()) {
230:               const sessionFile = join(sessionsDir, entry.name, "session.yaml");
231:               if (existsSync(sessionFile)) {
232:                 const content = readFileSync(sessionFile, "utf-8");
233:                 const data = load(content) as SessionData;
234:                 // Handle migration from checkoutPath to agentWorkspacePath
235:                 const sessionData = {
236:                   ...data,
237:                   agentWorkspacePath: data.agentWorkspacePath || (data as any).checkoutPath,
238:                 };
239:                 if (data.assignedAgentId === agentId) {
240:                   sessions.push({
241:                     ...sessionData,
242:                     createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
243:                     updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
244:                   });
245:                 }
246:               }
247:             }
248:           }
249:         }
250:       }
251:     }
252: 
253:     return sessions.sort((a, b) => b.createdAt.getTime() - a.createdAt.getTime());
254:   }
255: 
256:   async update(sessionId: string, updates: Partial<Omit<SessionData, "id" | "createdAt">>): Promise<Session | null> {
257:     const session = await this.findById(sessionId);
258:     if (!session) return null;
259: 
260:     const updatedData: SessionData = {
261:       ...session,
262:       ...updates,
263:       updatedAt: new Date().toISOString(),
264:     };
265: 
266:     const filePath = this.getSessionFilePath(session.projectId, sessionId);
267:     writeFileSync(filePath, dump(updatedData), "utf-8");
268: 
269:     return {
270:       ...updatedData,
271:       createdAt: new Date(updatedData.createdAt),
272:       updatedAt: new Date(updatedData.updatedAt),
273:     };
274:   }
275: 
276:   async delete(projectId: string, sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
277:     const sessionPath = this.getSessionPath(projectId, sessionId);
278:     
279:     // Delete entire session directory (includes upstream/, agent-workspace/, repo.fossil, session.yaml)
280:     if (existsSync(sessionPath)) {
281:       this.deleteDirectoryRecursive(sessionPath);
282:     }
283:   }
284: 
285:   private deleteDirectoryRecursive(dirPath: string): void {
286:     if (!existsSync(dirPath)) return;
287: 
288:     const entries = readdirSync(dirPath, { withFileTypes: true });
289:     
290:     for (const entry of entries) {
291:       const entryPath = join(dirPath, entry.name);
292:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
293:         this.deleteDirectoryRecursive(entryPath);
294:       } else {
295:         unlinkSync(entryPath);
296:       }
297:     }
298: 
299:     rmdirSync(dirPath);
300:   }
301: 
302:   async exists(projectId: string, sessionId: string): Promise<boolean> {
303:     return existsSync(this.getSessionFilePath(projectId, sessionId));
304:   }
305: }

    const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "up"], agentWorkspacePath);
    return {

  // Patch-based sync methods

  async generatePatch(
    agentWorkspacePath: string,
    fromCommit: string,
    toCommit: string
  ): Promise<VCSResult> {
    const result = await this.execCommand(
      ["fossil", "diff", "--from", fromCommit, "--to", toCommit, "-v"],
      agentWorkspacePath
    );

    return {
      success: result.success,
      output: result.output,
      error: result.error || undefined,
    };
  }

  async getCurrentCommit(agentWorkspacePath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
    const result = await this.execCommand(
      ["fossil", "sql", "SELECT hash FROM leaf WHERE rid = (SELECT value FROM tagxref WHERE tagid = (SELECT tagid FROM tag WHERE tagname = 'sym-trunk') ORDER BY mtime DESC LIMIT 1);"],
      agentWorkspacePath
    );

    if (result.success && result.output) {
      // Extract hash from SQL output
      const hash = result.output.trim();
      return {
        success: true,
        output: hash,
      };
    }

    // Fallback: get the current checkout version
    const infoResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "info"], agentWorkspacePath);
    if (infoResult.success) {
      const match = infoResult.output.match(/checkout:\s+([a-f0-9]+)/);
      if (match) {
        return {
          success: true,
          output: match[1],
        };
      }
    }

    return {
      success: false,
      error: result.error || "Failed to get current commit",
    };
  }

  async getFirstCommit(agentWorkspacePath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
    // Get the oldest commit in the current checkout's history
    const result = await this.execCommand(
      ["fossil", "sql", "SELECT uuid FROM blob WHERE rid = (SELECT objid FROM event ORDER BY mtime ASC LIMIT 1);"],
      agentWorkspacePath
    );

    if (result.success && result.output) {
      const hash = result.output.trim();
      return {
        success: true,
        output: hash,
      };
    }

    // Fallback: get the root commit
    const timelineResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "timeline", "-n", "0"], agentWorkspacePath);
    if (timelineResult.success) {
      const lines = timelineResult.output.split("\n");
      // Find the last line with a commit hash (oldest commit)
      for (let i = lines.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
        const match = lines[i].match(/\[([a-f0-9]+)\]/);
        if (match) {
          return {
            success: true,
            output: match[1],
          };
        }
      }
    }

    return {
      success: false,
      error: result.error || "Failed to get first commit",
    };
  }

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/src/vcs/index.ts

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-09 02:52:05
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/vcs/index.ts
newString:       return {
